# Codebase Review Ledger

This ledger tracks systematic review work across `lotus-core`.

Companion process document:

- [CODEBASE-REVIEW-PLAYBOOK.md](./CODEBASE-REVIEW-PLAYBOOK.md)

## Review entries

| Review ID | Date | Scope / Pattern | Status | Findings | Actions Taken | Follow-up | Evidence / Sign-off |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| CR-001 | 2026-03-10 | Async orchestration, heavy-gate runtime, quiescence barriers | Hardened | Post-RFC-081 heavy validation exposed real orchestration defects: duplicate position-timeseries fan-out, incorrect same-day aggregation re-arm semantics, quiescence false positives, and stale runtime assumptions in test-stack orchestration. | Hardened timeseries orchestration, added quiescence-aware cleanup with quiet-window support, removed false-positive blockers from quiescence, tightened E2E setup to wait for business-complete states, and refreshed failure-recovery evidence. | Keep watching CI/main heavy gates. If hosted CI shows environment-specific regressions, treat them as extensions of this scope until stabilized. | Commits `96a17a9`, `a5e4288`; local validation: `pytest tests/e2e -q -x -s` => `56 passed`; `python scripts/failure_recovery_gate.py --build --enforce` passed; RFC 081 reopened for hardening. |
| CR-002 | 2026-03-10 | Portfolio aggregation eligibility query shape | Hardened | `find_and_claim_eligible_jobs()` in portfolio aggregation/timeseries repositories allowed a correlated subquery to degrade into an accidental `FROM daily_position_snapshots, portfolio_aggregation_jobs` pattern. This prevented first eligible portfolio-day jobs from being claimed on a fresh workflow. | Rewrote the prior-day and completeness gates to use explicit `select(1)` correlation and correlated snapshot subqueries. Added unit query-shape tests and DB-backed integration coverage for first-day, mixed-epoch, and prior-day eligibility behavior. | Converge duplicate repository implementations so the same SQL is not maintained in two places. | Commits within `96a17a9`; tests: `tests/unit/services/timeseries_generator_service/.../test_unit_timeseries_repo.py`, `tests/unit/services/portfolio_aggregation_service/repositories/test_timeseries_repository.py`, `tests/integration/services/timeseries_generator_service/test_timeseries_repository_integration.py`; `tests/e2e/test_5_day_workflow.py` => `6 passed`. |
| CR-003 | 2026-03-10 | Cashflow replay correctness and epoch-versioned persistence | Hardened | Back-dated replay and stale-event flows could fail because cashflows were not safely versioned across epochs. Lower-level contract coverage was insufficient for replay-oriented persistence behavior. | Added epoch-versioned cashflow persistence support, updated cashflow consumer/runtime behavior, added integration tests for query-side cashflow repository behavior, and added unit tests for the consumer/manager paths. | Review remaining replay-sensitive repositories for the same epoch-versioning assumptions. | Commit `8a32e00`; migration `d1e2f3a4b5c6_feat_allow_epoch_versioned_cashflows.py`; query integration and cashflow consumer unit tests. |
| CR-004 | 2026-03-10 | Valuation scheduling for current-day positions | Hardened | Current-day market prices were not always creating the required valuation work deterministically. This left heavy workflows dependent on indirect or lagging triggers. | Updated valuation repositories and price-event trigger logic, then later removed the dead duplicate trigger surface from `position_valuation_calculator` once ownership was finalized in CR-091. | Keep valuation trigger ownership in `valuation_orchestrator_service`; do not reintroduce calculator-local scheduling paths. | Commit `f262393`; enduring evidence: `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_valuation_job_repository.py`; live ownership finalized in [CR-091-POSITION-VALUATION-WORKER-OWNERSHIP-CLEANUP.md](./CR-091-POSITION-VALUATION-WORKER-OWNERSHIP-CLEANUP.md). |
| CR-005 | 2026-03-10 | Test-stack environment, ports, and module isolation | Hardened | The previous Docker-backed test harness mixed fixed-port assumptions, shared compose project names, and weak cleanup semantics. This reduced confidence and created false negatives. | Introduced dynamic runtime allocation, project-scoped compose usage, Kafka readiness, quiescence-based cleanup, and corrected E2E setup/wait behavior. | Consider splitting full-stack E2E from smaller Docker-backed integration profiles to reduce runtime cost further. | Tests under `tests/test_support/`; `tests/conftest.py`; local `e2e-all`, `integration-all`, and failure-recovery gate all green. |
| CR-006 | 2026-03-10 | Duplicate repository and service logic across split services | Hardened | Review confirmed the real structural duplication was in repository pairs, not in consumer managers. `ValuationRepository` was duplicated in full between `valuation_orchestrator_service` and `position_valuation_calculator`. `TimeseriesRepository` was near-duplicated between `portfolio_aggregation_service` and `timeseries_generator_service`, with only a worker-local `get_position_timeseries(...)` difference. | Extracted shared valuation query/claim logic into `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py` and shared timeseries query/claim logic into `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/timeseries_repository_base.py`. Reduced all four service-local repository files to thin wrappers that preserve import paths, service-local metric hooks, and the worker-only `get_position_timeseries(...)` helper. Validated both converged paths with unit and integration repository suites. | Watch for future duplication in runtime scaffolding, but repository-body convergence for the reviewed valuation/timeseries pairs is complete. Do not force consumer-manager unification unless later review shows reusable scaffolding with a real payoff. | Evidence: [CR-006-DUPLICATE-REPOSITORY-REVIEW.md](./CR-006-DUPLICATE-REPOSITORY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/timeseries_repository_base.py`; service-local repository wrappers; valuation and timeseries repository unit/integration tests. |
| CR-007 | 2026-03-10 | Failure-recovery gate semantics | Hardened | Review confirmed the gate is evaluating bounded recovery, not strict full drain. A run can pass while `drain_seconds_to_baseline = timeout` if backlog age and DLQ/replay pressure recover within allowed bounds. That behavior is coherent, but it was previously ambiguous in the gate output. | Added explicit recovery classification to the gate result: `FULLY_DRAINED`, `BOUNDED_RECOVERY`, `FAILED_RECOVERY`. Added direct unit tests for the gate decision matrix and updated the review note accordingly. | If policy tuning is desired later, revisit thresholds separately. The semantic ambiguity is now closed. | Evidence: [CR-007-FAILURE-RECOVERY-REVIEW.md](./CR-007-FAILURE-RECOVERY-REVIEW.md); `tests/unit/scripts/test_failure_recovery_gate.py` => `12 passed`; `ruff check` passed on gate + tests; report `output/task-runs/20260310T050658Z-failure-recovery-gate.md`. |
| CR-008 | 2026-03-10 | Control-plane job health query shape | Hardened | The issue in `query_service` support/operations endpoints was query fan-out, not missing worker indexes. One overview/SLO request executed many separate aggregates over the same valuation and aggregation job tables. Existing indexed columns (`portfolio_id`, `status`, business-date columns) are broadly adequate for the current control-plane predicates. | Consolidated valuation and aggregation job health into combined summary queries and updated `OperationsService` to consume those summaries. Added unit coverage for the summary-query repository methods and the updated service interface. | If hosted runtime metrics later show true DB pressure on worker claim paths, review those separately under a scheduler/backlog performance batch. Do not add speculative indexes before evidence exists. | Evidence: [CR-008-CONTROL-PLANE-JOB-HEALTH-QUERY-REVIEW.md](./CR-008-CONTROL-PLANE-JOB-HEALTH-QUERY-REVIEW.md); `src/services/query_service/app/repositories/operations_repository.py`; `src/services/query_service/app/services/operations_service.py`; unit tests on repository + service summary behavior. |
| CR-009 | 2026-03-10 | Query vs query-control-plane source ownership | Hardened | RFC 81 split the runtime/API surface correctly, but control-plane source ownership was still blurred: `query_control_plane_service` imported routers and enterprise-readiness logic directly from `query_service`, and control-plane tests were split across `query_service` paths. | Moved control-plane router modules into `src/services/query_control_plane_service/app/routers/`, moved router dependency tests into `tests/integration/services/query_control_plane_service/`, moved router unit tests into `tests/unit/services/query_control_plane_service/routers/`, added service-local enterprise-readiness middleware for the control-plane app, updated `query_control_plane_service/app/main.py` to import only local app modules for that API surface, and removed the stale control-plane router copies from `src/services/query_service/app/routers/`. | Shared DTO/service/query logic may still remain in `query_service` where that is the canonical business/query layer. If later review shows a reusable shared query package is warranted, handle that as a separate convergence batch rather than re-blurring control-plane app ownership. | Evidence: [CR-009-QUERY-CONTROL-PLANE-OWNERSHIP-REVIEW.md](./CR-009-QUERY-CONTROL-PLANE-OWNERSHIP-REVIEW.md); local control-plane router package; moved control-plane unit/integration router tests; `tests/integration/services/query_control_plane_service/*` app-contract + dependency suites; `tests/unit/services/query_control_plane_service/routers/*`. |
| CR-010 | 2026-03-10 | Worker claim-path scheduler and backlog semantics | Hardened | Worker claim paths already use sound locking/claim semantics (`FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` with atomic claim updates) for valuation, aggregation, and reprocessing jobs. The main residual structural risk is duplicated claim repository code, already tracked in `CR-006`. One concrete inconsistency did exist: aggregation stale-job resets did not refresh `updated_at` while valuation stale-job resets did. | Reviewed worker claim implementations and stale-reset paths. Hardened both aggregation repository copies so stale resets now set `updated_at = now()` in addition to resetting status. Added unit coverage for the reset statement shape. | Converge duplicated valuation and aggregation repositories under `CR-006` so future claim-path fixes land once. Consider consistent reset metrics across worker types later. | Evidence: [CR-010-WORKER-CLAIM-PATH-REVIEW.md](./CR-010-WORKER-CLAIM-PATH-REVIEW.md); `src/services/timeseries_generator_service/app/repositories/timeseries_repository.py`; `src/services/portfolio_aggregation_service/app/repositories/timeseries_repository.py`; unit repository tests for stale reset. |
| CR-013 | 2026-03-10 | Financial calculator engine scope and ownership | Hardened | 
inancial-calculator-engine is not dead, but only its core/ and logic/ layers are truly shared. The ngine/ layer (TransactionProcessor + recalculation metrics) was only used by cost_calculator_service, so it was service-owned orchestration disguised as shared engine code. | Moved TransactionProcessor and recalculation monitoring into cost_calculator_service, moved the direct transaction-processor unit test into the service test area, updated manifest/doc references, and removed the dead 
inancial-calculator-engine/src/engine/ package. | If the remaining shared library is renamed later, do it as a dedicated vocabulary/package-governance slice. The current ownership fix is sufficient without broader package churn. | Evidence: [CR-013-FINANCIAL-CALCULATOR-ENGINE-SCOPE-REVIEW.md](./CR-013-FINANCIAL-CALCULATOR-ENGINE-SCOPE-REVIEW.md); src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/transaction_processor.py; src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/monitoring.py; moved transaction-processor unit tests. |
| CR-014 | 2026-03-10 | Startup/runtime contracts for dependency-critical services | Hardened | The hot-path startup review found that `ingestion_service` tolerated Kafka producer initialization failure by logging a fatal error and continuing startup with `app_state[\"kafka_producer\"] = None`. That let a write-ingress service advertise readiness while unable to fulfill its core publish contract. | Hardened `ingestion_service` to fail fast on Kafka producer initialization failure and added lifecycle-level integration coverage asserting startup raises when Kafka initialization fails. | Continue the same review pattern across other dependency-critical services; only treat dependency failure as degraded if the service contract is truly still valid. | Evidence: [CR-014-STARTUP-RUNTIME-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md](./CR-014-STARTUP-RUNTIME-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md); `src/services/ingestion_service/app/main.py`; `tests/integration/services/ingestion_service/test_ingestion_main_app_contract.py`. |
| CR-015 | 2026-03-10 | Web worker startup/runtime contract convergence | Hardened | Web-backed worker services were all implementing the same startup/metrics/runtime/shutdown pattern in their own `main.py` files. The duplication had already drifted into inconsistent fatal-error semantics: some workers re-raised `ConsumerManager` failures, others logged critical errors and exited without re-raising. | Extracted the shared runtime contract into `portfolio_common.worker_runtime.run_instrumented_worker_service(...)`, migrated the web-backed worker services onto it, and standardized fatal worker runtime failures to log and re-raise consistently. Added direct unit tests for the shared helper. | Review remaining non-web worker mains separately. Do not force `persistence_service` or pure HTTP services into this helper unless their contracts genuinely converge. | Evidence: [CR-015-WEB-WORKER-STARTUP-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md](./CR-015-WEB-WORKER-STARTUP-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/worker_runtime.py`; updated worker `main.py` files; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_worker_runtime.py`. |
| CR-016 | 2026-03-10 | Pure HTTP app bootstrap duplication | Hardened | The pure HTTP/control-plane apps (`query_service`, `query_control_plane_service`, `event_replay_service`, `financial_reconciliation_service`, `ingestion_service`) repeated a large shared bootstrap pattern: Prometheus exposure, OpenAPI metrics override/enrichment, correlation/request/trace middleware, HTTP observability middleware, exception normalization, and health-router registration. | Extracted the shared layer into `portfolio_common.http_app_bootstrap` and migrated the five HTTP apps onto it while keeping service-local ownership for enterprise middleware, lifespan/startup behavior, dependency-critical startup policy, health dependency sets, and router selection. Validated the migrated apps with their existing app-contract suites. | If future convergence is needed, extend only the shared middleware/OpenAPI/router-registration layer. Do not turn the helper into a generic app factory unless startup contracts truly converge. | Evidence: [CR-016-PURE-HTTP-BOOTSTRAP-REVIEW.md](./CR-016-PURE-HTTP-BOOTSTRAP-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/http_app_bootstrap.py`; app mains for query, query-control-plane, event-replay, financial-reconciliation, and ingestion; `pytest` app-contract suites for query, query-control-plane, event-replay, and ingestion => `25 passed`. |
| CR-017 | 2026-03-10 | Financial engine dead config/runtime surface | Hardened | The engine still contained an orphaned `core/config/settings.py` layer describing app/runtime settings for a standalone API that no longer existed in `lotus-core`. The module had no live production/test/script imports, but it kept `pydantic-settings` and `python-dotenv` in the dependency graph. | Removed the dead `core/config/settings.py` module and dropped the now-unused engine-package dependencies. | `core/enums/cost_method.py` was reviewed in CR-018. Remaining live engine ownership was finalized later in CR-020. | Evidence: [CR-017-FINANCIAL-ENGINE-DEAD-CONFIG-REVIEW.md](./CR-017-FINANCIAL-ENGINE-DEAD-CONFIG-REVIEW.md). |
| CR-018 | 2026-03-10 | Cost-basis vocabulary ownership and alias control | Hardened | `cost_basis_method` was still live business vocabulary, but the only explicit enum lived in `cost-calculator-service engine package` and had become dead after config cleanup. The live repo surface also mixed canonical `AVCO` with stale alias `AVERAGE_COST`. | Promoted cost-basis vocabulary into `portfolio-common`, updated live portfolio/event/consumer paths to use it, normalized persistence writes around the canonical enum, added regression tests for canonical values and explicit rejection of stale alias values, and removed the dead engine-local enum. | Do not add compatibility aliases unless the project later has a real external backward-compatibility obligation. | Evidence: [CR-018-COST-BASIS-VOCABULARY-REVIEW.md](./CR-018-COST-BASIS-VOCABULARY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/cost_basis.py`; persistence + sell-linkage + cost-consumer updates; new unit/integration tests. |
| CR-019 | 2026-03-10 | Financial engine model surface ownership | Hardened | The remaining engine still carried dead standalone request/response models and vague top-level `core/` and `logic/` source trees. Only `Transaction` and `ErroredTransaction` were still live models. | Repackaged the live engine into a meaningful `domain/` and `processing/` structure, kept only the live models, and deleted dead `request.py` / `response.py` plus the obsolete generic source files. | Final service ownership was completed in CR-020 once production usage confirmed the engine was no longer truly shared. | Evidence: [CR-019-FINANCIAL-ENGINE-MODEL-SURFACE-REVIEW.md](./CR-019-FINANCIAL-ENGINE-MODEL-SURFACE-REVIEW.md). |
| CR-020 | 2026-03-10 | Cost engine ownership finalization | Hardened | After CR-019, the remaining production imports of the cost engine were all inside `cost_calculator_service`. The package was no longer genuinely shared, so keeping it under `src/libs` created a false architectural boundary. | Folded the engine into `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/cost_engine`, moved engine unit tests under service ownership, removed the obsolete `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/cost_engine/` package, and updated current-state docs/runtime tooling to match. | Update historical RFC references opportunistically when those RFCs are touched again. Current-state code and living docs now reflect the correct ownership boundary. | Evidence: [CR-020-COST-ENGINE-OWNERSHIP-FINALIZATION.md](./CR-020-COST-ENGINE-OWNERSHIP-FINALIZATION.md); `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/cost_engine/*`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/engine/*`; `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/Dockerfile`; `scripts/test_manifest.py`. |
| CR-021 | 2026-03-10 | Docker image preflight and local runtime drift | Hardened | Docker-backed heavy tests still assumed required base images were already present locally, which caused late compose failures when `cp-zookeeper` / `cp-kafka` images were missing. `docker-compose.yml` also still carried a stale `financial-calculator-engine` volume mount after CR-020 removed that package. | Added Docker image preflight/pull behavior to `tests/test_support/docker_stack.py`, added unit coverage for missing-image and failed-pull cases, and removed the stale `financial-calculator-engine` volume mount from `cost_calculator_service` in `docker-compose.yml`. | If image sourcing becomes a recurring problem, define explicit mirror/cache warm-up policy in dev/CI bootstrap. The concrete local runtime drift reviewed here is now closed. | Evidence: [CR-021-DOCKER-IMAGE-PREFLIGHT-REVIEW.md](./CR-021-DOCKER-IMAGE-PREFLIGHT-REVIEW.md); `tests/test_support/docker_stack.py`; `tests/unit/test_support/test_docker_stack.py`; `docker-compose.yml`. |
| CR-022 | 2026-03-10 | Unit-test async cleanup warning debt | Hardened | Branch-scoped unit premerge runs still emitted `aclose()`-not-awaited warnings from test doubles around `get_async_db_session`, plus one Kafka payload-format test that exercised DB recording even though DB persistence was not the behavior under test. | Replaced raw async-generator monkeypatches with explicit single-yield async iterators in the affected tests, mocked `_record_consumer_dlq_event` in the Kafka payload-format test, and re-ran the warning-producing tests with warnings enabled to prove the warnings were gone. | Keep future async cleanup warnings classified as test-harness debt first unless a targeted reproduction proves a production resource-lifecycle bug. | Evidence: [CR-022-UNIT-TEST-ASYNC-CLEANUP-WARNING-REVIEW.md](./CR-022-UNIT-TEST-ASYNC-CLEANUP-WARNING-REVIEW.md); warning-producing unit tests rerun clean with `-W default`. |
| CR-023 | 2026-03-10 | Unit Kafka producer noise and stale legacy test leftovers | Hardened | The unit manifest still printed noisy librdkafka connection failures because the unit tier allowed accidental construction of the real `confluent_kafka.Producer`. The repo also still had three stale legacy analytics test directories that only contained `__pycache__` leftovers. | Added a unit-tier autouse fixture that monkeypatches `portfolio_common.kafka_utils.Producer` to a `MagicMock` and resets the producer singleton before/after each unit test, added explicit producer shutdown support in `portfolio_common.kafka_utils`, re-ran the full unit manifest to prove the suite is quiet, and removed the stale legacy test directories. | If future tests need a real Kafka client, move them to integration coverage instead of weakening the unit tier. | Evidence: [CR-023-UNIT-KAFKA-PRODUCER-NOISE-REVIEW.md](./CR-023-UNIT-KAFKA-PRODUCER-NOISE-REVIEW.md); `tests/unit/conftest.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/kafka_utils.py`; `python scripts/test_manifest.py --suite unit --quiet` => `893 passed, 6 deselected` with no producer-noise stderr. |
| CR-024 | 2026-03-10 | Disabled-endpoint compatibility residue | Hardened | `src/services/query_service/app/routers/legacy_gone.py` was dead compatibility residue. No production route imported it, no integration or E2E behavior depended on it, and only its own unit test plus a few historical RFCs still referenced it. | Deleted the dead helper and its unit test, then updated historical RFCs so they point to the surviving disabled-route evidence: route inventory and shared E2E assertions. | Continue removing fake compatibility surfaces when runtime ownership is gone. Keep only route-inventory and shared-assertion evidence for disabled-endpoint policy. | Evidence: [CR-024-DISABLED-ENDPOINT-COMPATIBILITY-RESIDUE-REVIEW.md](./CR-024-DISABLED-ENDPOINT-COMPATIBILITY-RESIDUE-REVIEW.md); `tests/integration/services/query_service/test_main_app.py` => `9 passed`. |
| CR-025 | 2026-03-10 | Cost-basis documentation drift in transaction specs | Hardened | Multiple transaction specs still advertised `LIFO`, `AVERAGE_COST`, `SPECIFIC_ID`, or `SPECIFIC_LOT` as active lotus-core cost-basis policies even though the code now supports only canonical `FIFO` and `AVCO`. That created direct documentation drift against runtime behavior. | Updated the affected transaction specs to reflect the actual supported policies and canonical vocabulary. | Continue removing unsupported policy names from current-state docs unless and until the implementation actually supports them. | Evidence: `docs/rfc-transaction-specs/transactions/SELL/RFC-SELL-01.md`; `docs/rfc-transaction-specs/transactions/misc/RFC-REDEMPTION-01 Canonical Fixed Income Redemption Family Specification.md`; `docs/rfc-transaction-specs/transactions/FX/RFC-FX-01 Canonical FX Transaction Specification.md`. |
| CR-026 | 2026-03-10 | OpenAPI and vocabulary governance baseline | In Review | Baseline RFC-0067 scan shows the current `openapi_quality_gate.py` and `api_vocabulary_inventory.py --validate-only` already pass. The remaining gap is quality depth, not basic compliance: Swagger/example richness needs to become an explicit review stream, and the only alias-like code hit found was sanctioned header aliasing for `X-Correlation-ID`. | Added this workstream to the review program and established the baseline evidence for future OpenAPI/example hardening slices. | Target richer request/response examples and schema descriptions on services where the gate is only minimally satisfied, while keeping no-alias governance enforced for API-facing contracts. | Evidence: `python scripts/openapi_quality_gate.py` => pass; `python scripts/api_vocabulary_inventory.py --validate-only` => pass; alias scan limited to header alias usage in `financial_reconciliation_service`. |
| CR-027 | 2026-03-10 | Financial reconciliation Swagger depth | Hardened | `financial_reconciliation_service` already passed the OpenAPI gate, but it still relied too heavily on operation-level examples. Field-level schema descriptions and parameter documentation were inconsistent, which made Swagger usable but not gold-standard. | Added field-level descriptions/examples across reconciliation request and response DTOs, enriched header/query parameter documentation, documented 404 response examples for `GET /reconciliation/runs/{run_id}`, and added an OpenAPI contract test that asserts the schema contains the richer documentation. | Continue the same pass across the other active HTTP services, starting with the weakest control-plane surfaces. | Evidence: [CR-027-FINANCIAL-RECONCILIATION-SWAGGER-DEPTH-REVIEW.md](./CR-027-FINANCIAL-RECONCILIATION-SWAGGER-DEPTH-REVIEW.md); `python -m pytest tests/integration/services/financial_reconciliation_service/test_financial_reconciliation_app.py -q` => `7 passed`; OpenAPI gate and vocabulary inventory still pass. |
| CR-028 | 2026-03-10 | Event replay Swagger depth | Hardened | `event_replay_service` already had operation-level examples, but the main operational endpoints still under-documented path/query filters and common error responses. That made the OpenAPI surface less useful for operators despite passing the baseline gate. | Added descriptions/examples for the highest-value operational path and query parameters, documented `404`/`409` response examples on the main replay endpoints, and added an OpenAPI integration test that asserts those parameters and error examples are present. | Continue the same pass on the next active HTTP surface with the thinnest remaining Swagger depth. | Evidence: `src/services/event_replay_service/app/routers/ingestion_operations.py`; `tests/integration/services/event_replay_service/test_event_replay_app.py` => `7 passed`; OpenAPI gate and vocabulary inventory still pass. |
| CR-029 | 2026-03-10 | Query control-plane operations Swagger depth | Hardened | `query_control_plane_service` already exposed the right support/lineage operations, but path/query parameter examples and 404 response examples were too thin for an operator-facing control-plane API. | Added explicit path/query parameter descriptions/examples and documented 404 response examples on the support overview, calculator SLO, valuation job, aggregation job, and lineage endpoints. | CR-030 | 2026-03-10 | Simulation Swagger depth | Hardened | `query_control_plane_service` simulation endpoints were functionally correct but still under-documented: path parameters had no examples, not-found/invalid-state responses lacked concrete examples, and the shared DTO schema depth was thin. | Added field-level schema descriptions/examples to shared simulation DTOs, enriched simulation router path parameter docs and response examples, and added an OpenAPI integration assertion that locks the richer contract in place. | Continue the same Swagger-depth pass on the next weakest active HTTP surface. | CR-031 | 2026-03-10 | Analytics inputs Swagger depth | Hardened | The analytics-input surface already had good shared DTOs, but the control-plane router still lacked explicit path parameter docs and concrete operator-facing error examples on the highest-value portfolio/export endpoints. | Added path parameter descriptions/examples and concrete `400`/`404`/`422` response examples to the analytics-input control-plane router, then added an OpenAPI integration assertion to lock those docs in place. | Continue the same depth pass on the next weakest active HTTP surface. | CR-086 | 2026-03-11 | Current-state ownership evidence drift | Hardened | A few current-state docs still used `query_control_plane_service/app/main.py` or other service mains as ownership evidence for behavior that is actually implemented in concrete router modules. That weakened traceability in standards and the RFC index. | Replaced the weak evidence references with the live router-level ownership paths in `durability-consistency.md` and the RFC-081 index row. | Keep future implementation evidence pointed at the concrete owning module unless the startup contract itself is the subject. | Evidence: [CR-086-CURRENT-STATE-OWNERSHIP-EVIDENCE-DRIFT-REVIEW.md](./CR-086-CURRENT-STATE-OWNERSHIP-EVIDENCE-DRIFT-REVIEW.md); `docs/standards/durability-consistency.md`; `docs/RFCs/RFC-INDEX.md`. |
| CR-087 | 2026-03-11 | Stale control epoch emission | Hardened | The durable `FINANCIAL_RECONCILIATION` control-stage row was already monotonic, and the read path already chose the latest epoch. The remaining gap was that an older reconciliation completion could still publish a stale `PortfolioDayControlsEvaluated` event after a newer epoch already existed for the same portfolio-day. | Added latest-epoch resolution to `PipelineStageRepository` and suppressed stale control-event emission in `PipelineOrchestratorService` when the incoming completion is not for the latest epoch. Added unit and integration coverage for the stale-vs-latest epoch invariant. | Apply the same review pattern to any future control-plane event that persists multiple epochs for the same business scope: durable monotonicity is not enough if emission semantics are still stale. | Evidence: [CR-087-STALE-CONTROL-EPOCH-EMISSION-REVIEW.md](./CR-087-STALE-CONTROL-EPOCH-EMISSION-REVIEW.md); `src/services/pipeline_orchestrator_service/app/services/pipeline_orchestrator_service.py`; `src/services/pipeline_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/pipeline_stage_repository.py`; `tests/unit/services/pipeline_orchestrator_service/services/test_pipeline_orchestrator_service.py`; `tests/integration/services/pipeline_orchestrator_service/test_int_pipeline_stage_repository.py`. |
| CR-088 | 2026-03-11 | Stale valuation epoch job creation | Hardened | `ValuationJobRepository.upsert_job(...)` previously accepted any epoch for a given `(portfolio_id, security_id, valuation_date)` scope, so an older readiness event could still create or re-arm obsolete valuation work after a newer epoch already existed. | Added latest-epoch resolution to `ValuationJobRepository` and skipped stale older-epoch upserts when a newer epoch already exists for the same valuation scope. Added unit and DB-backed integration coverage for the stale-vs-latest valuation job invariant. | Apply the same stale-epoch review to any other scheduler/work-set repository that keys work by business scope plus epoch. | Evidence: [CR-088-STALE-VALUATION-EPOCH-JOB-REVIEW.md](./CR-088-STALE-VALUATION-EPOCH-JOB-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_valuation_job_repository.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_valuation_repo.py`. |
| CR-089 | 2026-03-11 | Current-epoch valuation trigger selection | Hardened | The immediate price-event path used `find_open_position_keys_for_security_on_date(...)`, which previously returned any open epoch for a key as of the target date. That meant obsolete historical epochs could still be selected as valuation work candidates even when `PositionState` had advanced the key to a newer current epoch. | Tightened `find_open_position_keys_for_security_on_date(...)` to join against `PositionState` and return only the current epoch for each active key. Added DB-backed integration coverage proving mixed historical epochs resolve to the current epoch only. | Apply the same ownership rule to any work-candidate query: if a key has a canonical current-state owner, candidate generation must align with that owner instead of inferring “latest enough” from history alone. | Evidence: [CR-089-CURRENT-EPOCH-VALUATION-TRIGGER-REVIEW.md](./CR-089-CURRENT-EPOCH-VALUATION-TRIGGER-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_valuation_repo.py`. |
| CR-090 | 2026-03-11 | Epoch-fenced watermark advance | Hardened | `bulk_update_states(...)` updated `PositionState` rows by key only, so a scheduler pass that observed epoch `N` could still overwrite the newer current row after the key had already advanced to epoch `N+1`. This was a stale-writer race on canonical current state, not merely stale job creation. | Added `expected_epoch` fencing to `bulk_update_states(...)`, updated the valuation scheduler implementations to pass the observed epoch through with each watermark/status advance, and added unit coverage proving stale expected epochs do not overwrite newer rows and scheduler updates carry the observed epoch. | Apply the same epoch-fence rule to any other bulk state mutation path that derives writes from an earlier scheduler snapshot. | Evidence: [CR-090-EPOCH-FENCED-WATERMARK-ADVANCE-REVIEW.md](./CR-090-EPOCH-FENCED-WATERMARK-ADVANCE-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/position_state_repository.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_position_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-091 | 2026-03-11 | Position valuation worker ownership cleanup | Hardened | `position_valuation_calculator` was already a pure worker runtime, but it still carried dead scheduler, reprocessing-worker, readiness-consumer, price-event-consumer, and worker-local settings files from before the valuation split. These paths were no longer wired into the service runtime and risked future fixes landing in the wrong service. | Deleted the dead orchestration/runtime residue and the orphaned worker-local tests, corrected current-state schema catalog references to the live `valuation_orchestrator_service` ownership surface, fixed stale copied path headers in the surviving orchestrator files, and restored the still-valid consumer/scheduler/reprocessing tests under `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/` so coverage follows the live owner. | Keep `position_valuation_calculator` worker-only. Any future scheduling or replay logic belongs in `valuation_orchestrator_service`, not the worker service. | Evidence: [CR-091-POSITION-VALUATION-WORKER-OWNERSHIP-CLEANUP.md](./CR-091-POSITION-VALUATION-WORKER-OWNERSHIP-CLEANUP.md); `src/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/app/consumer_manager.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/consumer_manager.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/consumers/*`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/*`; `docs/Database-Schema-Catalog.md`. |
| CR-092 | 2026-03-11 | Stale reprocessing job recovery | Hardened | `reprocessing_jobs` tracked attempt metadata but had no stale `PROCESSING` reset path. A dead `ReprocessingWorker` could therefore leave `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs stuck forever, unlike valuation and aggregation jobs which already had stale-processing recovery. | Added `ReprocessingJobRepository.find_and_reset_stale_jobs(timeout_minutes=15)`, wired `ReprocessingWorker` to run that recovery step before claiming the next batch, and added unit coverage for repository stale-reset behavior and worker ordering. | If reprocessing job types expand later, keep them on the same durable stale-reset contract rather than adding type-specific recovery behavior ad hoc. | Evidence: [CR-092-STALE-REPROCESSING-JOB-RECOVERY-REVIEW.md](./CR-092-STALE-REPROCESSING-JOB-RECOVERY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/reprocessing_worker.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/test_reprocessing_worker.py`. |
| CR-093 | 2026-03-11 | Position state mutation timestamp integrity | Hardened | `PositionState` is the canonical replay/watermark state table, but its two replay-critical mutation paths did not explicitly refresh `updated_at`. That left timestamp integrity dependent on implicit ORM/update behavior rather than explicit state mutation intent. | Added `updated_at=func.now()` to `increment_epoch_and_reset_watermark(...)` and `update_watermarks_if_older(...)`, and extended DB-backed repository tests to assert the mutated rows keep a populated timestamp. | Keep current-state timestamp fields explicit on all future repository mutation statements instead of relying on implicit column `onupdate` behavior. | Evidence: [CR-093-POSITION-STATE-MUTATION-TIMESTAMP-INTEGRITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-093-POSITION-STATE-MUTATION-TIMESTAMP-INTEGRITY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/position_state_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_position_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-094 | 2026-03-11 | Position consumer replay boundary | Hardened | `TransactionEventConsumer` already distinguished stage-gate payloads from replay/original transaction payloads, but there was no explicit unit-level proof that replay payloads bypass canonical transaction lookup while preserving replay epoch and idempotency behavior. | Added consumer-level tests proving the replay path bypasses canonical lookup, preserves the incoming epoch, and still marks idempotency on the direct replay contract path. | Keep future consumer changes aligned to the same boundary: stage-gate events may hydrate canonical rows; replay payloads should not. | Evidence: [CR-094-POSITION-CONSUMER-REPLAY-BOUNDARY-REVIEW.md](./CR-094-POSITION-CONSUMER-REPLAY-BOUNDARY-REVIEW.md); `src/services/calculators/position_calculator/app/consumers/transaction_event_consumer.py`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/position_calculator/consumers/test_position_calculator_consumer.py`. |
| CR-095 | 2026-03-11 | Replay correlation propagation | Hardened | `TransactionEventConsumer.process_message(...)` assumed the Kafka runtime had already populated `correlation_id_var`. That was true inside `BaseConsumer.run()`, but false for direct consumer invocation paths, so replay-path idempotency records could fall back to `"<not-set>"` even when message headers already carried a real `correlation_id`. | Extracted reusable header resolution into `BaseConsumer._resolve_message_correlation_id(...)`, updated `TransactionEventConsumer` to set/reset correlation context locally when direct paths do not already have it, and added tests proving replay and stage-gate direct execution persist the Kafka header correlation. | Apply the same pattern to any other consumer whose `process_message(...)` can be invoked directly outside `BaseConsumer.run()`; direct-path audit fidelity should not depend on runtime-loop side effects. | Evidence: [CR-095-REPLAY-CORRELATION-PROPAGATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-095-REPLAY-CORRELATION-PROPAGATION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/kafka_consumer.py`; `src/services/calculators/position_calculator/app/consumers/transaction_event_consumer.py`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/position_calculator/consumers/test_position_calculator_consumer.py`. |
| CR-096 | 2026-03-11 | Direct consumer correlation context | Hardened | The same direct-path correlation assumption from CR-095 existed more broadly in control-plane and valuation consumers: they read `correlation_id_var` inside `process_message(...)` without ensuring the context had been initialized locally. That could silently degrade audit/idempotency fidelity on direct invocation paths. | Added shared `BaseConsumer._message_correlation_context(...)` to unify current-context reuse, header resolution, deterministic fallback ids, and payload-correlation preference. Applied it to the reviewed high-value control-plane and valuation consumers and extended direct consumer tests accordingly. | Continue applying the same helper to any remaining consumer whose `process_message(...)` is intentionally invoked directly in tests or in-process replay/control paths. | Evidence: [CR-096-DIRECT-CONSUMER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-REVIEW.md](./CR-096-DIRECT-CONSUMER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/kafka_consumer.py`; reviewed consumer files under `valuation_orchestrator_service`, `financial_reconciliation_service`, and `pipeline_orchestrator_service`; corresponding unit tests. |
| CR-097 | 2026-03-11 | Watermark advance mismatch visibility | Hardened | Epoch fencing in `bulk_update_states(...)` prevents stale overwrites, but the valuation scheduler still treated partial advancement as routine success. That made stale-epoch skips safe but operationally invisible. | Updated `ValuationScheduler._advance_watermarks(...)` to warn when fewer rows are advanced than were prepared, including prepared/updated/skipped counts and sample keys. Added unit coverage for the partial-advance warning path. | If later metrics work is needed, expose the stale-skipped count as explicit telemetry. The immediate observability gap is now closed at log/test level. | Evidence: [CR-097-WATERMARK-ADVANCE-MISMATCH-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-097-WATERMARK-ADVANCE-MISMATCH-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/test_valuation_scheduler.py`. |
| CR-098 | 2026-03-11 | Terminal reprocessing normalization | Hardened | The valuation scheduler only considered lagging keys (`watermark_date < latest_business_date`), so a key could remain `status="REPROCESSING"` even after its watermark had already reached the latest business date. That left stale control state and undercounted the reprocessing gauge. | Added `get_terminal_reprocessing_states(...)` to the valuation repository and updated the scheduler to normalize terminal `REPROCESSING` rows back to `CURRENT` via epoch-fenced bulk updates. Added unit coverage for the normalization path. | If later operational reporting needs to distinguish genuinely active reprocessing from just-normalized terminal residue, expose the normalized count as explicit telemetry rather than inferring it indirectly. | Evidence: [CR-098-TERMINAL-REPROCESSING-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-098-TERMINAL-REPROCESSING-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/test_valuation_scheduler.py`. |
| CR-099 | 2026-03-12 | Terminal reprocessing normalization visibility | Hardened | CR-098 corrected stale terminal `REPROCESSING` rows by normalizing them back to `CURRENT`, but the normalization path still treated partial success as routine. Because `bulk_update_states(...)` is epoch-fenced, terminal normalization can legitimately skip stale rows once a newer epoch already exists. That is safe, but leaving it silent weakens runtime diagnosability in the same way CR-097 previously did for watermark advancement. | Updated `ValuationScheduler._advance_watermarks(...)` to warn when fewer terminal reprocessing states are normalized than were prepared, including prepared count, updated count, stale-skipped count, and sample keys. Added unit coverage for the partial-normalization warning path. | If this path becomes operationally noisy, surface the skipped count as explicit telemetry rather than removing the warning. | Evidence: [CR-099-TERMINAL-REPROCESSING-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-099-TERMINAL-REPROCESSING-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/test_valuation_scheduler.py`. |
| CR-100 | 2026-03-12 | Reprocessing fan-out stale skip visibility | Hardened | `ReprocessingWorker` fans out watermark resets across all portfolios holding a security, but its success logging treated partial updates as routine success. Because `PositionStateRepository.update_watermarks_if_older(...)` can legitimately skip rows when newer or already-older state exists, epoch/current-state fencing could silently reduce the actual fan-out without any runtime signal. | Updated `ReprocessingWorker._process_batch()` to warn when fewer watermark resets are applied than were targeted, including targeted count, updated count, stale-skipped count, and sample keys. Added unit coverage for the partial fan-out warning path. | If this path becomes noisy in production, expose the skipped count as explicit telemetry instead of removing the warning. | Evidence: [CR-100-REPROCESSING-FANOUT-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-100-REPROCESSING-FANOUT-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/reprocessing_worker.py`; `tests/unit/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/core/test_reprocessing_worker.py`. |
| CR-101 | 2026-03-12 | Back-dated replay duplicate-trigger deduplication | Hardened | When a back-dated original transaction triggered epoch bump and replay, `PositionCalculator.calculate(...)` always appended the triggering event after loading historical transactions from the database. If the triggering transaction had already been persisted to the canonical transaction table, it was replayed twice in the same epoch. | Deduplicated the replay batch by `transaction_id` before appending the triggering event, preserving deterministic ordering while preventing double replay of the same canonical transaction. Added unit coverage for the persisted-trigger replay case. | If future replay flows can legitimately emit the same `transaction_id` with different semantic payloads, deduplication must move to a stronger replay-key contract. For the current canonical transaction model, `transaction_id` is the correct replay identity. | Evidence: [CR-101-BACKDATED-REPLAY-DEDUP-REVIEW.md](./CR-101-BACKDATED-REPLAY-DEDUP-REVIEW.md); `src/services/calculators/position_calculator/app/core/position_logic.py`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/position_calculator/core/test_position_logic.py`. |
| CR-102 | 2026-03-12 | DB-backed replay deduplication proof | Hardened | CR-101 fixed duplicate replay of a persisted triggering transaction at the unit level, but the invariant still needed proof on the real atomic outbox path. Without a DB-backed assertion, the system could regress while still appearing correct under mocks. | Added an integration test that persists the triggering back-dated transaction, runs the real atomic replay path, and asserts the outbox batch contains each `transaction_id` only once. | If future replay batching evolves beyond transaction identity, extend the proof to the stronger replay-key contract rather than relying only on `transaction_id` uniqueness. | Evidence: [CR-102-DB-BACKED-REPLAY-DEDUP-PROOF.md](./CR-102-DB-BACKED-REPLAY-DEDUP-PROOF.md); `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_atomicity.py`. |
| CR-103 | 2026-03-12 | Replay outbox correlation preservation | Hardened | The back-dated replay path created durable outbox events without explicitly propagating the active correlation context into the outbox row. That meant the replay payload could be correct while the durable outbox lineage still lost the triggering correlation id. | Updated `PositionCalculator.calculate(...)` to persist the active `correlation_id_var` value on replay outbox events when present, and added both unit and DB-backed integration coverage proving the outbox rows retain that correlation. | Apply the same durability test pattern to any other outbox-backed replay or fan-out path that currently relies on ambient context rather than explicit outbox correlation propagation. | Evidence: [CR-103-REPLAY-OUTBOX-CORRELATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-103-REPLAY-OUTBOX-CORRELATION-REVIEW.md); `src/services/calculators/position_calculator/app/core/position_logic.py`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/position_calculator/core/test_position_logic.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_atomicity.py`. |
| CR-104 | 2026-03-12 | Dead timeseries scheduler residue | Hardened | After the RFC 81 service split, `timeseries_generator_service` still carried a dead `AggregationScheduler` copy and test even though scheduling ownership had moved to `portfolio_aggregation_service`. | CR-105 | 2026-03-12 | Calculator consumer direct-path correlation context | Hardened | Three calculator consumers could be invoked directly without `BaseConsumer.run()`, but still assumed `correlation_id_var` had already been initialized by the runtime loop. | CR-107 | 2026-03-12 | Persistence consumer direct-path correlation context | Hardened | `GenericPersistenceConsumer` still relied on ambient `correlation_id_var` state for durable outbox/idempotency writes, even though persistence consumers are invoked directly in unit and in-process paths. | CR-108 | 2026-03-12 | Shared direct-consumer correlation helper convergence | Hardened | `PriceEventConsumer` and `TransactionEventConsumer` still implemented direct-path correlation handling manually even after the shared helper existed. That preserved correct behavior but left the contract inconsistent by implementation, increasing drift risk. | Replaced the manual context setup in both consumers with `_message_correlation_context(...)` and verified behavior against the existing direct-path unit suites. | Keep direct consumer correlation handling on the shared helper path.
