| CR-109 | 2026-03-12 | Cost reprocessing consumer direct-path correlation context | Hardened | `cost_calculator_service` still had one unreviewed direct-invocation consumer: `ReprocessingConsumer`. It republished transactions through `ReprocessingRepository`, but its `process_message(...)` path still relied on ambient `correlation_id_var` state instead of explicitly adopting the Kafka header correlation id. | Wrapped the consumer body in `_message_correlation_context(...)` and added unit coverage proving the repository executes under the header-provided correlation id during direct invocation. | Keep any future replay/reprocessing consumer on the same shared correlation-context contract. Direct paths must not depend on `BaseConsumer.run()` side effects for durable audit lineage. | Evidence: [CR-109-COST-REPROCESSING-CONSUMER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-REVIEW.md](./CR-109-COST-REPROCESSING-CONSUMER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-REVIEW.md); `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/consumers/reprocessing_consumer.py`; `tests/unit/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/consumer/test_reprocessing_consumer.py`. |
| CR-110 | 2026-03-12 | Set-based `position_state` bulk updates | Hardened | `PositionStateRepository.bulk_update_states(...)` was still issuing one SQL `UPDATE` per row. That preserved correctness, but it was not a gold-standard shape for a hot control table mutated by the valuation scheduler and replay normalization paths. | Replaced the row-by-row loop with a single set-based epoch-fenced update using a derived values table, while preserving the `(portfolio_id, security_id, expected_epoch)` fence and explicit `updated_at = now()` semantics. Added multi-row timestamp integrity coverage. | Keep future bulk control-table mutations set-based unless there is a specific reason not to. Per-row loops on scheduler hot paths should be treated as a performance smell by default. | Evidence: [CR-110-SET-BASED-POSITION-STATE-BULK-UPDATE-REVIEW.md](./CR-110-SET-BASED-POSITION-STATE-BULK-UPDATE-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/position_state_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_position_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-111 | 2026-03-12 | Reprocessing request ordering determinism | Hardened | `ReprocessingRepository.reprocess_transactions_by_ids(...)` queried `transaction_id IN (...)` with no ordering. That made multi-transaction replay requests nondeterministic even though the API accepts an ordered list of transaction ids. | Added explicit ordering by caller-provided `transaction_ids` and added unit coverage proving republished message order matches request order. | Preserve deterministic replay order whenever a replay API accepts multiple ids or events. Row-return order from the database is not a valid replay contract. | Evidence: [CR-111-REPROCESSING-REQUEST-ORDERING-REVIEW.md](./CR-111-REPROCESSING-REQUEST-ORDERING-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_repository.py`. |
| CR-112 | 2026-03-12 | Reprocessing request duplicate-ID deduplication | Hardened | CR-111 fixed deterministic ordering for multi-transaction replay requests, but the replay API still accepted duplicate transaction IDs and would republish the same canonical transaction multiple times in one request. That is a real replay-correctness gap, not just inefficiency. | Deduplicated caller-provided `transaction_ids` while preserving first-seen order before querying and republishing, and added unit coverage proving duplicate IDs result in one republish per canonical transaction in deterministic order. | Keep replay request handling idempotent at the API boundary. If future replay workflows need explicit duplicate semantics, define that as a separate contract rather than falling out of raw input lists. | Evidence: [CR-112-REPROCESSING-REQUEST-DEDUP-REVIEW.md](./CR-112-REPROCESSING-REQUEST-DEDUP-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_repository.py`. |
| CR-113 | 2026-03-12 | Replay API correlation header hygiene | Hardened | The replay API boundary now preserved deterministic ordering and deduplicated duplicate transaction ids, but it still treated the default `correlation_id_var` value `"<not-set>"` as a real correlation header. That could republish replay messages with poisoned lineage metadata even though no real correlation id had been established. | Normalized `"<not-set>"` to `None` before constructing Kafka headers and added unit coverage proving replay publication omits the correlation header when the ambient context is unset. | Apply the same normalization rule to any remaining publication paths that still convert ambient correlation context directly into durable headers. | Evidence: [CR-113-REPLAY-API-CORRELATION-HYGIENE-REVIEW.md](./CR-113-REPLAY-API-CORRELATION-HYGIENE-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_repository.py`. |
| CR-114 | 2026-03-12 | Write-plane lineage sentinel normalization | Hardened | The ingestion write plane still treated the default context sentinel `"<not-set>"` as real lineage metadata. That could leak into Kafka headers and acknowledgement/request-lineage payloads even when no real correlation, request, or trace id had been established. | Normalized `"<not-set>"` to `None` in `IngestionService._get_headers(...)` and in `get_request_lineage()`, then added unit coverage for both the Kafka-header path and the shared request-lineage helper. | Apply the same sentinel-normalization rule to any other remaining API-layer helpers that echo ambient lineage context directly into durable or client-visible metadata. | Evidence: [CR-114-WRITE-PLANE-LINEAGE-SENTINEL-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-114-WRITE-PLANE-LINEAGE-SENTINEL-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md); `src/services/ingestion_service/app/services/ingestion_service.py`; `src/services/ingestion_service/app/request_metadata.py`; ingestion-service unit tests. |
| CR-115 | 2026-03-12 | Enterprise readiness lineage sentinel normalization | Hardened | Both enterprise-readiness middleware implementations still treated the default ambient context sentinel `"<not-set>"` as a real correlation id. That meant deny/write audit events could record poisoned client-visible lineage metadata even when no real correlation id had been established. | Added correlation normalization in both enterprise-readiness implementations so `None`, empty string, and `"<not-set>"` collapse to `None` before audit emission, and added unit coverage for deny and successful write audit paths in both owners. | Apply the same normalization rule to any remaining middleware or API helpers that echo ambient lineage state into logs, audits, or client-visible metadata. | Evidence: [CR-115-ENTERPRISE-READINESS-LINEAGE-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-115-ENTERPRISE-READINESS-LINEAGE-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md); query-service and query-control-plane enterprise readiness modules; corresponding unit tests. |
| CR-116 | 2026-03-12 | Reprocessing ingress duplicate suppression | Hardened | The replay API consumer and repository were already being hardened for deterministic ordering and duplicate suppression, but the ingress router still accepted duplicate transaction IDs and published duplicate `transactions.reprocessing.requested` commands before the downstream layers saw them. | Deduplicated caller-provided `transaction_ids` at ingress while preserving first-seen order, and used the deduplicated list consistently for rate limiting, job accepted count, persisted request payload, publication, and failure bookkeeping. Added router-level integration coverage proving duplicate IDs produce one command per canonical transaction. | Keep replay request deduplication at the earliest boundary possible. Downstream consumers may still defend themselves, but ingress should not knowingly inject duplicate commands. | Evidence: [CR-116-REPROCESSING-INGRESS-DUPLICATE-SUPPRESSION-REVIEW.md](./CR-116-REPROCESSING-INGRESS-DUPLICATE-SUPPRESSION-REVIEW.md); `src/services/ingestion_service/app/routers/reprocessing.py`; `tests/integration/services/ingestion_service/test_ingestion_routers.py`. |
| CR-117 | 2026-03-12 | Reset-watermarks durable job coalescing | Hardened | Repeated instrument-level reprocessing triggers for the same security could create multiple pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs even before the worker claimed the first one. That inflated the durable queue with redundant work and weakened recovery determinism. | `ReprocessingJobRepository.create_job(...)` now coalesces pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs by `security_id`, updating the pending job to the earliest impacted date instead of creating duplicates. Added unit coverage for both same/later-date coalescing and earlier-date merge behavior. | If duplicate fanout pressure still shows up under production load, consider a database-level uniqueness contract for pending reset-watermarks jobs keyed by `(job_type, payload->>security_id)` instead of relying only on repository behavior. | Evidence: [CR-117-RESET-WATERMARKS-JOB-COALESCING-REVIEW.md](./CR-117-RESET-WATERMARKS-JOB-COALESCING-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-118 | 2026-03-12 | Instrument reprocessing trigger priority order | Hardened | Instrument-level replay triggers were claimed by `updated_at` only. Under backlog, that lets row recency override the actual business priority, which is the oldest impacted date. | `ValuationRepositoryBase.get_instrument_reprocessing_triggers(...)` now orders by `earliest_impacted_date`, then `updated_at`, then `security_id`, and a DB-backed integration test proves the scheduler-facing order is oldest-impact-first. | If replay backlog becomes large enough to need explicit fairness guarantees, consider exposing queue-age and oldest-impacted-date telemetry directly rather than relying only on deterministic ordering. | Evidence: [CR-118-INSTRUMENT-REPROCESSING-PRIORITY-ORDER-REVIEW.md](./CR-118-INSTRUMENT-REPROCESSING-PRIORITY-ORDER-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_instrument_reprocessing_repo.py`. |
| CR-119 | 2026-03-12 | Reset-watermarks worker claim priority order | Hardened | After CR-118, instrument-level triggers were prioritized by oldest impacted date, but the durable `RESET_WATERMARKS` worker queue still claimed work by `created_at` only. That left the replay pipeline with inconsistent priority once work crossed the durable queue boundary. | `ReprocessingJobRepository.find_and_claim_jobs(...)` now claims `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs by `(payload->>'earliest_impacted_date')::date`, then `created_at`, then `id`, while leaving other job types on the generic created-at order. Added repository tests locking both query branches. | If the durable queue later needs stronger starvation protection across job types, move from job-type-specific ordering to an explicit priority model instead of relying on implicit SQL branches. | Evidence: [CR-119-RESET-WATERMARKS-WORKER-CLAIM-PRIORITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-119-RESET-WATERMARKS-WORKER-CLAIM-PRIORITY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-120 | 2026-03-12 | Dead instrument reprocessing repository ownership | Hardened | `InstrumentReprocessingStateRepository` still existed in both `valuation_orchestrator_service` and `position_valuation_calculator`, but only the valuation orchestrator copy was live. The worker-local duplicate represented dead alternate ownership for an active replay-trigger contract. | Deleted the dead `position_valuation_calculator` copy and kept ownership singular under `valuation_orchestrator_service`, where back-dated price-event replay triggers actually originate. | Keep instrument-level replay trigger ownership singular. If the repository ever becomes truly shared again, move it to a real shared package instead of restoring service-local duplicates. | Evidence: [CR-120-DEAD-INSTRUMENT-REPROCESSING-REPOSITORY-OWNERSHIP-REVIEW.md](./CR-120-DEAD-INSTRUMENT-REPROCESSING-REPOSITORY-OWNERSHIP-REVIEW.md); deleted `src/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; live owner remains `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-121 | 2026-03-12 | Historical reset-watermarks duplicate normalization | Hardened | CR-117 prevented new duplicate pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs through the repository, but historical duplicates could still already exist in the durable queue and would eventually be processed redundantly by the worker. | Added `normalize_pending_reset_watermarks_duplicates()` and invoked it before `RESET_WATERMARKS` claim. The queue now keeps one pending row per `security_id`, updates the keeper to the minimum impacted date, and deletes redundant pending rows. Added repository tests that lock the normalization and claim sequencing. | If duplicate residue still matters operationally, surface the deleted-count as explicit replay queue telemetry rather than relying only on the log line. | Evidence: [CR-121-HISTORICAL-RESET-WATERMARKS-DUPLICATE-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-121-HISTORICAL-RESET-WATERMARKS-DUPLICATE-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-122 | 2026-03-12 | DB-backed reset-watermarks normalization proof | Hardened | CR-121 hardened the repository logic, but the durable queue behavior still needed proof against the real database path. Without that, normalization remained a unit-level claim rather than a demonstrated SQL contract. | Added DB-backed integration coverage proving duplicate pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` rows collapse to one row per security with the earliest impacted date, while other job types remain untouched by the normalization logic. | Keep durable replay queue semantics proven below the worker layer. If the SQL changes again, this proof should fail before E2E is needed. | Evidence: [CR-122-DB-BACKED-RESET-WATERMARKS-NORMALIZATION-PROOF.md](./CR-122-DB-BACKED-RESET-WATERMARKS-NORMALIZATION-PROOF.md); `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-123 | 2026-03-12 | Instrument trigger coalescing DB proof | Hardened | The live `InstrumentReprocessingStateRepository` is the durable source of instrument-level replay triggers, but its coalescing behavior had not been proven against the real database path. Repeated back-dated price events could have regressed into multiple rows or widened impacted dates without being caught below scheduler/E2E level. | Added DB-backed integration coverage proving repeated upserts leave one trigger row per security and preserve the earliest impacted date, and corrected the stale module header so the file reflects its real owner path. | Keep the trigger-source contract proven below the scheduler layer. If the trigger model evolves, extend these tests rather than relying on scheduler behavior to catch source drift. | Evidence: [CR-123-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-COALESCING-DB-PROOF.md](./CR-123-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-COALESCING-DB-PROOF.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; `tests/integration/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/test_instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-124 | 2026-03-12 | Fenced instrument trigger deletion | Hardened | `ValuationScheduler` converted fetched instrument-level triggers into durable `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs and then deleted trigger rows by `security_id` only. A newer back-dated price event could lower the impacted date between fetch and delete, letting an older scheduler cycle erase the newer replay requirement. | Changed trigger deletion to use `(security_id, earliest_impacted_date)` fences, updated the scheduler to pass the fetched trigger state instead of raw ids, and added DB-backed proof that a stale delete cannot remove a trigger row whose impacted date was lowered after fetch. | Keep trigger consumption fenced by fetched state, not just identity. If trigger rows later gain more mutable state, extend the fence rather than regressing to identity-only deletes. | Evidence: [CR-124-FENCED-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-DELETION-REVIEW.md](./CR-124-FENCED-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-DELETION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_instrument_reprocessing_repo.py`. |
| CR-125 | 2026-03-12 | Pending reset-watermarks uniqueness | Hardened | Duplicate pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` work was already coalesced and normalized in repository logic, but the durable queue still relied on Python behavior rather than schema enforcement. A direct insert path or future regression could still reintroduce duplicate pending replay jobs for the same security. | Added an Alembic migration that normalizes historical duplicate pending rows and creates a partial unique index on pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs by `payload->>'security_id'`. Added DB-backed integration coverage proving the database rejects a second pending row for the same security. | Keep replay-critical uniqueness in the schema where possible. Repository coalescing should remain as the ergonomic path, but the durable queue invariant must now be treated as a DB contract. | Evidence: [CR-125-PENDING-RESET-WATERMARKS-UNIQUENESS-REVIEW.md](./CR-125-PENDING-RESET-WATERMARKS-UNIQUENESS-REVIEW.md); `alembic/versions/e4f5a6b7c8d9_feat_add_pending_reset_watermarks_uniqueness.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-126 | 2026-03-12 | Atomic reset-watermarks creation | Hardened | CR-125 strengthened the queue by enforcing uniqueness in the database, but `ReprocessingJobRepository.create_job(...)` still used a read-then-insert/update pattern. Under concurrency, that could race into an integrity failure instead of coalescing replay intent. | Replaced the read-then-write path with one SQL upsert that inserts or merges a pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` job and returns the surviving row. Added unit and DB-backed integration coverage proving repeated creation leaves one pending row with the earliest impacted date. | Keep schema-backed uniqueness paired with atomic repository behavior. Once the database owns the invariant, repository code should use one atomic write path rather than a best-effort read-modify-write sequence. | Evidence: [CR-126-ATOMIC-RESET-WATERMARKS-CREATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-126-ATOMIC-RESET-WATERMARKS-CREATION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-127 | 2026-03-12 | Typed instrument trigger upsert | Hardened | The instrument trigger source was already atomic, but it still embedded the incoming impacted date inside raw SQL text for the `LEAST(...)` merge expression. That was weaker than the queue path we just hardened and left an avoidable raw-SQL seam on an active replay boundary. | Replaced the string-built `LEAST(...)` expression with a typed SQLAlchemy `func.least(...)` upsert using `stmt.excluded.earliest_impacted_date`, while preserving explicit `updated_at = now()` semantics. Re-ran the DB-backed trigger repository proof to verify behavior stayed correct. | Keep replay-trigger upserts typed and explicit. Atomicity alone is not enough; the merge expression should be structurally owned in code rather than assembled from raw SQL fragments. | Evidence: [CR-127-TYPED-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-UPSERT-REVIEW.md](./CR-127-TYPED-INSTRUMENT-TRIGGER-UPSERT-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; `tests/integration/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/test_instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`. |
| CR-128 | 2026-03-12 | Latest processing-date fallback for scheduler normalization | Hardened | The valuation scheduler assumed `business_dates` always exists. In real workflows, valuation jobs and snapshots can complete without that table being seeded, leaving `get_latest_business_date()` as `None`. That made watermark advancement and terminal `REPROCESSING -> CURRENT` normalization a no-op even though the data plane was already complete. | Changed `ValuationRepository.get_latest_business_date()` to fall back to the latest observed valuation-processing date from `daily_position_snapshots` and `portfolio_valuation_jobs` when the business calendar is empty. Added DB-backed repository proof and reran the exact AVCO -> cashflow E2E sequence that had been leaking `REPROCESSING` state across module cleanup. | Use the business calendar as the primary source of truth, but do not let an empty calendar strand durable replay state when actual valuation work has already completed. Scheduler normalization needs a deterministic latest-processing-date fallback. | Evidence: [CR-128-LATEST-PROCESSING-DATE-FALLBACK-REVIEW.md](./CR-128-LATEST-PROCESSING-DATE-FALLBACK-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_valuation_repo.py`; `tests/e2e/test_5_day_workflow.py`; `tests/e2e/test_avco_workflow.py`; `tests/e2e/test_cashflow_pipeline.py`. |
| CR-129 | 2026-03-12 | Quiescence active-row activity window | Hardened | The quiescence snapshot already excluded non-blocking work correctly, but the quiet-window timestamp still read the max `updated_at` across whole blocking tables. That let historical completed rows hold the quiet window open even when the live blocking snapshot was all zeros, causing false E2E cleanup timeouts. | Changed `read_pipeline_last_activity_at()` to apply the same blocking predicates used by the live snapshot when computing last activity time, and added unit proof that non-blocking and inactive rows do not influence the quiet window. | Keep quiescence logic symmetric: the activity-time window must be derived from the same live blocking set as the snapshot counts, otherwise cleanup becomes sensitive to unrelated historical churn. | Evidence: [CR-129-QUIESCENCE-ACTIVE-ROW-ACTIVITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-129-QUIESCENCE-ACTIVE-ROW-ACTIVITY-REVIEW.md); `tests/test_support/pipeline_quiescence.py`; `tests/unit/test_support/test_pipeline_quiescence.py`. |
| CR-130 | 2026-03-12 | Typed replay-job date binding | Hardened | CR-126 moved pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` creation onto one atomic upsert, but the real asyncpg path still treated the impacted date parameter as ambiguous. The repository contract was correct in shape but not fully valid on the actual driver path. | Explicitly bound `security_id` as `String` and `earliest_impacted_date` as `Date`, and executed the upsert with a parsed `date` value. DB-backed integration proof now passes on the real asyncpg path. | Replay queue hardening is only complete once the atomic path is proven on the real driver, not just in unit tests or abstract SQL form. | Evidence: [CR-130-TYPED-REPLAY-JOB-DATE-BINDING-REVIEW.md](./CR-130-TYPED-REPLAY-JOB-DATE-BINDING-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_job_repository.py`. |
| CR-131 | 2026-03-12 | Integration cleanup contract for replay queue | Hardened | `clean_db` truncated most durable state but omitted `reprocessing_jobs`, so integration tests on the replay queue could inherit historical pending/processing rows and fail for the wrong reason. That made repository tests appear flaky when the issue was test-harness residue. | Added `reprocessing_jobs` to the global truncate list in `tests/conftest.py` and revalidated the replay-job integration suite plus the full integration tier. | Keep `TABLES_TO_TRUNCATE` aligned with every durable control/work queue table as new infrastructure tables are introduced. | Evidence: `tests/conftest.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_reprocessing_job_repository.py`; full `python -m pytest tests/integration -x -q` run green on branch. |
| CR-132 | 2026-03-12 | E2E identity collision and predicate correctness | Hardened | Two broad-suite E2E failures were caused by test-contract issues rather than runtime defects: `test_fx_lifecycle` used a strict-subset check instead of true key containment, and `test_timeseries_pipeline` reused static portfolio/security/transaction identifiers that collided across the full suite. | Fixed the FX cash-position predicate to use `issubset`, randomized the timeseries fixture identifiers with a per-module suffix, and revalidated the exact files plus the full `tests/e2e` tier. | Keep E2E scenarios on unique identities by default and treat broad-suite failures as possible contract-collision defects before assuming pipeline regressions. | Evidence: `tests/e2e/test_fx_lifecycle.py`; `tests/e2e/test_timeseries_pipeline.py`; full `python -m pytest tests/e2e -x -q` run green on branch. |
| CR-133 | 2026-03-12 | Durable replay correlation lineage | Hardened | Back-dated price events preserved correlation on the immediate valuation-job path, but the durable replay chain still lost it: `instrument_reprocessing_state` carried no correlation id and coalesced `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs carried no correlation id. That weakened auditability exactly where durable replay should be strongest. | Added nullable `correlation_id` to both `instrument_reprocessing_state` and `reprocessing_jobs`, propagated the price-event correlation through trigger upsert and scheduler job creation, and proved the earliest impacted trigger owns the persisted correlation on both the trigger row and the durable replay job. | Continue treating durable control rows as first-class lineage records. If future replay intents are coalesced by another key, carry correlation through the durable trigger and the durable job, not just transient event payloads. | Evidence: [CR-125-DURABLE-REPLAY-CORRELATION-LINEAGE-REVIEW.md](./CR-125-DURABLE-REPLAY-CORRELATION-LINEAGE-REVIEW.md); `alembic/versions/f0a1b2c3d4e5_feat_add_replay_correlation_lineage.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; trigger/scheduler unit tests; DB-backed trigger/job integration tests. |
| CR-134 | 2026-03-12 | Coalesced replay lineage backfill | Hardened | Durable replay lineage was preserved when a newer event lowered the impacted date, but it was still dropped when the stored trigger/job row had `correlation_id = NULL` and a later duplicate for the same impacted date arrived with a real correlation id. That left coalesced replay state under-audited even though enough lineage had become available. | Updated both trigger coalescing and pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` job coalescing so `NULL` correlation ids are backfilled from later same-date duplicates, and added DB-backed proofs for both paths. | Treat missing lineage on durable coalesced rows as recoverable state, not as final truth. If better lineage arrives for the same business impact, the durable row should absorb it. | Evidence: [CR-134-COALESCED-REPLAY-LINEAGE-BACKFILL-REVIEW.md](./CR-134-COALESCED-REPLAY-LINEAGE-BACKFILL-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; DB-backed trigger/job integration tests. |
| CR-135 | 2026-03-12 | Reprocessing worker correlation context and dead helper removal | Hardened | Durable replay correlation was preserved on disk, but `ReprocessingWorker` still processed claimed `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs outside the job's correlation context. At the same time, `ValuationRepositoryBase.find_portfolios_for_security(...)` had become dead after the worker switched to date-aware fanout and only survived through obsolete tests. | The worker now executes each durable replay job under `job.correlation_id` and restores ambient context afterward. Added unit proof for that context propagation. Removed the dead `find_portfolios_for_security(...)` helper and its obsolete integration test coverage. | Keep runtime lineage aligned with durable lineage. When a replay helper is no longer part of the real business path, delete it instead of letting old tests preserve fake ownership. | Evidence: [CR-135-REPROCESSING-WORKER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-AND-DEAD-HELPER-REVIEW.md](./CR-135-REPROCESSING-WORKER-CORRELATION-CONTEXT-AND-DEAD-HELPER-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/reprocessing_worker.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; reprocessing worker unit tests; valuation repository integration tests. |
| CR-136 | 2026-03-12 | Date-aware fanout latest-history proof | Hardened | The worker-facing date-aware replay fanout contract had proof for pre-impact closures and future opens, but not for the more realistic mixed case where a portfolio closes before the impacted date and reopens after it. Without that proof, a future query refactor could regress to “any historical holding” semantics. | Added a DB-backed integration test proving `find_portfolios_holding_security_on_date(...)` uses the latest history row on or before the impacted date: the portfolio is excluded while closed on the impacted date and included again after reopening. | Keep the replay fanout contract anchored to the latest holding state as of the impacted date, not any older positive holding record. | Evidence: [CR-136-DATE-AWARE-FANOUT-LATEST-HISTORY-PROOF.md](./CR-136-DATE-AWARE-FANOUT-LATEST-HISTORY-PROOF.md); `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_instrument_reprocessing_repo.py`. |
| CR-137 | Current-Epoch Date-Aware Fanout | Replay / valuation repository | Hardened | `valuation_repository_base.find_portfolios_holding_security_on_date(...)` now fences `PositionHistory` against the live `PositionState.epoch`, and DB-backed proofs now seed explicit current state rows so worker fanout follows the real control model. | `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py`; `tests/integration/services/calculators/position_valuation_calculator/test_int_instrument_reprocessing_repo.py`; `docs/architecture/CR-137-CURRENT-EPOCH-DATE-AWARE-FANOUT-REVIEW.md` |

That leaves unnecessary sort/scan pressure on active replay control tables under backlog. | `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/database_models.py`; `alembic/versions/f2b3c4d5e6f7_perf_add_replay_ordering_indexes.py`; `docs/architecture/CR-142-REPLAY-ORDERING-INDEX-REVIEW.md` |

| CR-152 | 2026-03-12 | Replay duplicate normalization observability | Hardened | Durable replay duplicate normalization had become a meaningful control path, but it was only visible through logs and tests. Operators could not see whether duplicate `RESET_WATERMARKS` rows were actively being collapsed under backlog pressure. | Added `reprocessing_duplicates_normalized_total{scope=...}` to the shared monitoring layer, emitted it from pending reset-watermarks normalization, and surfaced it in Grafana. | Keep future durable replay normalization paths on metric-backed observability, not log-only visibility. | Evidence: [CR-152-REPLAY-DUPLICATE-NORMALIZATION-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-152-REPLAY-DUPLICATE-NORMALIZATION-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/monitoring.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; `grafana/dashboards/portfolio_analytics.json`. |
| CR-153 | 2026-03-12 | Replay stale-skip observability | Hardened | The replay and scheduler paths already warned when epoch fencing caused partial updates, but stale-skip counts were not exported as metrics. That made replay pressure invisible unless operators searched logs. | Added `reprocessing_stale_skips_total{stage=...}` to the shared monitoring layer, emitted it from reset-watermarks fanout, watermark advancement, and terminal reprocessing normalization, and surfaced it in Grafana. | Keep stale-skip pressure metric-backed across replay/state-machine paths so operators can see recurring fence pressure before it becomes a support incident. | Evidence: [CR-153-REPLAY-STALE-SKIP-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-153-REPLAY-STALE-SKIP-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/monitoring.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/reprocessing_worker.py`; `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py`; `grafana/dashboards/portfolio_analytics.json`. |
| CR-154 | 2026-03-12 | Shared lineage normalization contract | Hardened | Sentinel lineage normalization was duplicated across transport, write-plane, replay, and audit code. That created drift risk for a banking-critical contract. | Added `normalize_lineage_value(...)` to `portfolio_common.logging_utils` and replaced local sentinel checks across the affected modules, with direct helper proof and affected-surface revalidation. | Keep lineage sentinel handling centralized. New transport or audit boundaries should reuse the shared helper instead of reintroducing local `"<not-set>"` checks. | Evidence: [CR-154-SHARED-LINEAGE-NORMALIZATION-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md](./CR-154-SHARED-LINEAGE-NORMALIZATION-CONTRACT-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/logging_utils.py`; affected write-plane, replay, transport, and audit modules. |
| CR-155 | 2026-03-12 | Outbox terminal failure and hot path | Hardened | `OutboxDispatcher` had `MAX_RETRIES` defined but did not enforce it. Permanently failing rows stayed `PENDING` forever and kept re-entering the live queue. The table also lacked the composite indexes that match the dispatcher's actual claim pattern. | Added terminal failure semantics so retry-threshold rows become `FAILED` instead of remaining `PENDING`, and added `(status, created_at)` plus `(status, last_attempted_at)` indexes for `outbox_events`. Added integration proof for the terminal transition. | If operators later need explicit alerting on terminal outbox failures, add a dedicated Prometheus metric for `FAILED` transitions rather than inferring only from logs. | Evidence: [CR-155-OUTBOX-TERMINAL-FAILURE-AND-HOT-PATH-REVIEW.md](./CR-155-OUTBOX-TERMINAL-FAILURE-AND-HOT-PATH-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/outbox_dispatcher.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/database_models.py`; `tests/integration/libs/portfolio-common/test_outbox_dispatcher.py`. |
| CR-156 | 2026-03-12 | Outbox backlog and terminal failure observability | Hardened | After CR-155, the dispatcher prevented permanently failing rows from poisoning the live queue, but operators still could not directly see durable `FAILED` residue or the age of the oldest pending row. Existing dashboards only exposed pending count plus published/failed/retried rates. | Added `outbox_events_failed_stored` and `outbox_events_oldest_pending_age_seconds`, updated the dispatcher gauge read to publish them, added DB-backed proof for the gauge contract, and surfaced both metrics on the existing Grafana outbox pressure panel. | If terminal-failure alerting is needed later, derive it from the durable-failure gauge rather than retry-rate heuristics. | Evidence: [CR-156-OUTBOX-BACKLOG-AND-TERMINAL-FAILURE-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-156-OUTBOX-BACKLOG-AND-TERMINAL-FAILURE-OBSERVABILITY-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/monitoring.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/outbox_dispatcher.py`; `tests/integration/libs/portfolio-common/test_outbox_dispatcher.py`; `grafana/dashboards/portfolio_analytics.json`. |
| CR-157 | 2026-03-13 | Coalesced replay lineage null-earlier-date preservation | Hardened | Durable replay coalescing still had one lineage-loss path: if an older impacted date arrived without a correlation id, it could replace a stored non-null correlation with `NULL` simply because the date was older. That weakened auditability on both the trigger row and the durable replay job. | Updated both trigger and `RESET_WATERMARKS` job coalescing so an earlier incoming row with `correlation_id = NULL` preserves an existing non-null durable correlation. Added DB-backed proofs for both paths. | Keep earliest business impact and best-known lineage as separate concerns. Older date should win ordering, but missing lineage should not erase already-known lineage. | Evidence: [CR-157-COALESCED-REPLAY-LINEAGE-NULL-EARLIER-DATE-REVIEW.md](./CR-157-COALESCED-REPLAY-LINEAGE-NULL-EARLIER-DATE-REVIEW.md); `src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/repositories/instrument_reprocessing_state_repository.py`; `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py`; replay lineage DB-backed integration tests. |

| CR-158 | 2026-03-13 | Stale reprocessing retry ceiling and model drift | Hardened | Durable RESET_WATERMARKS jobs could cycle between PROCESSING and PENDING forever after repeated worker crashes, and the SQLAlchemy model still carried the old invalid replay-ordering index expression even though the migration had already been corrected. | Added configurable REPROCESSING_WORKER_MAX_ATTEMPTS with a default of 3, changed stale replay recovery to mark over-limit jobs FAILED with a durable reason instead of resetting forever, passed that ceiling through ReprocessingWorker, and aligned the ReprocessingJob model index expression to the real migration contract. | If operators need explicit alerting on replay jobs that hit the retry ceiling, add a dedicated metric rather than relying only on logs and durable FAILED state. | Evidence: [CR-158-STALE-REPROCESSING-RETRY-CEILING-AND-MODEL-DRIFT-REVIEW.md](./CR-158-STALE-REPROCESSING-RETRY-CEILING-AND-MODEL-DRIFT-REVIEW.md); src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing_job_repository.py; src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/reprocessing_worker.py; src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/settings.py; src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/database_models.py; unit replay repository/worker proof. |

| CR-159 | 2026-03-13 | Valuation stale retry ceiling | Hardened | PortfolioValuationJob stale recovery still reset PROCESSING rows back to PENDING forever, leaving the valuation queue inconsistent with the replay queue after CR-158 and allowing repeated worker crashes to create infinite retry cycles. | Added configurable VALUATION_SCHEDULER_MAX_ATTEMPTS with default 3, changed stale valuation recovery to mark over-limit rows FAILED with a durable reason instead of resetting forever, and passed that ceiling through ValuationScheduler. | Apply the same terminal stale-retry symmetry to the aggregation queue so all durable control queues share one failure model. | Evidence: [CR-159-VALUATION-STALE-RETRY-CEILING-REVIEW.md](./CR-159-VALUATION-STALE-RETRY-CEILING-REVIEW.md); src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/valuation_repository_base.py; src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/core/valuation_scheduler.py; src/services/valuation_orchestrator_service/app/settings.py; valuation unit and DB-backed integration proof. |

| CR-162 | 2026-03-13 | Outbox runtime configurability | Hardened | `OutboxDispatcher` enforced terminal failure semantics, but the retry ceiling still lived as a hardcoded constant inside a shared durable component and the shared polling/batch policy was effectively buried in constructor defaults. | CR-165 | 2026-03-13 | Epoch fencer service ownership contract | Hardened | `EpochFencer` still allowed `service_name` to default to `"<not-set>"`, which meant a stale-epoch drop on an active replay/control path could silently lose real service ownership in the emitted metric. | Made `service_name` mandatory on `EpochFencer` construction and updated the shared unit proofs to require an explicit owner. | Keep service ownership explicit on control-path observability helpers; do not rely on sentinel defaults for metrics that drive operational triage. | Evidence: [CR-165-EPOCH-FENCER-SERVICE-OWNERSHIP-CONTRACT.md](./CR-165-EPOCH-FENCER-SERVICE-OWNERSHIP-CONTRACT.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/reprocessing.py`; `tests/unit/libs/portfolio-common/test_reprocessing.py`. |

| CR-169 | 2026-03-13 | Shared durable lineage boundary normalization | Hardened | Replay repositories had already been hardened against sentinel lineage, but other shared durable repositories still accepted raw `correlation_id` values. | CR-171 | 2026-03-13 | Reprocessing job model-schema uniqueness alignment | Hardened | The database already enforced a partial unique index for pending `RESET_WATERMARKS` jobs keyed by `payload->>'security_id'`, but the SQLAlchemy model still only declared the non-unique priority index. That left ORM metadata drifting away from the real durable replay invariant. | Added the missing partial unique index declaration to `ReprocessingJob` and added a metadata-level unit test proving the model advertises the same uniqueness contract as the migration-backed database. | Keep durable queue invariants aligned across migration history, ORM metadata, and tests. | CR-172 | 2026-03-13 | Direct consumer correlation context simplification | Hardened | Several direct-invocation consumers had already adopted `_message_correlation_context(...)`, but still re-read `correlation_id_var` inside the context body. | CR-173 | 2026-03-13 | Portfolio aggregation correlation context simplification | Hardened | `PortfolioTimeseriesConsumer` already used `_message_correlation_context(...)`, but still re-read `correlation_id_var` inside the context body. | CR-175 | 2026-03-13 | Control-plane queue pressure visibility | Hardened | Grafana exposed durable queue pressure for valuation and aggregation, but the support/control-plane API still exposed only partial job health. | CR-176 | 2026-03-13 | HTTP bootstrap lineage header normalization | Hardened | The shared pure-HTTP bootstrap middleware still trusted incoming lineage headers verbatim. If a caller sent `"<not-set>"` or an empty value, services echoed that sentinel back into response headers and log context instead of treating it as missing lineage. | Normalized incoming `X-Correlation-ID`, `X-Request-Id`, and `X-Trace-Id` through `normalize_lineage_value(...)`, generated fresh ids when the incoming values were missing or sentinel, and added integration proofs for `query_service`, `query_control_plane_service`, and `event_replay_service`. | Apply the same boundary rule to any non-HTTP transport that still accepts raw external lineage values before shared runtime or persistence handling. | Evidence: [CR-176-HTTP-BOOTSTRAP-LINEAGE-HEADER-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-176-HTTP-BOOTSTRAP-LINEAGE-HEADER-NORMALIZATION-REVIEW.md); `src/libs/portfolio-common/portfolio_common/http_app_bootstrap.py`; app-contract integration tests for query, control-plane, and replay services. |

| CR-177 | 2026-03-13 | Analytics export queue pressure visibility | Hardened | Analytics export is a durable queue with accepted, running, and failed states, but the support overview API exposed queue pressure only for valuation and aggregation. Operators using the control-plane HTTP surface could not see export backlog or failed export pressure. | Added analytics export queue health summary to `OperationsRepository`, extended `SupportOverviewResponse`/`OperationsService.get_support_overview(...)` with pending/running/stale/failed/backlog fields, and strengthened unit plus control-plane OpenAPI coverage. | If analytics export gets its own scheduler or retry model later, keep its queue pressure on the same first-class support surface as the other durable control queues. | Evidence: [CR-177-ANALYTICS-EXPORT-QUEUE-PRESSURE-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md](./CR-177-ANALYTICS-EXPORT-QUEUE-PRESSURE-VISIBILITY-REVIEW.md); operations repository/service/DTO files; `tests/unit/services/query_service/services/test_operations_service.py`; `tests/integration/services/query_control_plane_service/test_operations_router_dependency.py`; `tests/integration/services/query_control_plane_service/test_control_plane_app.py`. |

| CR-178 | 2026-03-13 | Analytics export hot-path index review | Hardened | Analytics export was promoted to a first-class durable queue on the support API, but the underlying table still exposed only single-column indexes even though the active queue and support scans filter by `portfolio_id`, `status`, `created_at`, and `updated_at`. | Added composite queue indexes for `(portfolio_id, status, created_at)` and `(status, updated_at)` at both ORM metadata and Alembic levels, with metadata-level proof in `test_database_models.py`. | Keep durable queue visibility and queue-path indexing aligned. | CR-179 | 2026-03-13 | Analytics export durable lifecycle review | Hardened | Analytics export jobs only persisted terminal failure state for expected `AnalyticsInputError` paths. An unexpected processing exception could roll back the entire job row and erase the durable support/audit record for that export attempt. | Refactored `AnalyticsTimeseriesService.create_export_job(...)` into explicit durable lifecycle steps: reserve job, mark running, and finalize complete or failed in separate transactions. Unexpected exceptions now persist a durable `failed` job with a stable error message before re-raising, and lower-level tests prove both expected and unexpected failure paths. | Keep durable job lifecycles explicit. | CR-180 | 2026-03-13 | Analytics export stale-running reuse contract | Hardened | Durable analytics export jobs could remain in `accepted` or `running` if a process died mid-request. The fingerprint reuse path would then keep reusing that stale row forever instead of superseding it with a new export attempt. | Added configurable `LOTUS_CORE_ANALYTICS_EXPORT_STALE_TIMEOUT_MINUTES` and changed analytics export reservation so completed jobs are reused, fresh accepted/running jobs are reused, and stale accepted/running jobs are first marked `failed` with a durable superseded reason before a new job is created. | CR-187 | 2026-03-13 | Support listing operational priority ordering | Hardened | Support-plane listings were still ordered mostly by recency, which is the wrong contract for live incident response. | CR-241 | 2026-03-14 | Stale reset overwrite race across replay, valuation, and aggregation workers | Hardened | Replay, valuation, and aggregation stale-reset paths all used a two-step `select stale rows -> update by id` flow without re-checking current ownership at update time. A worker could complete or re-claim a row between those steps, and the stale sweep could overwrite live durable state back to `PENDING` or `FAILED`. | Added update-time guards requiring `status = 'PROCESSING'` and `updated_at < stale_cutoff` in all three stale-reset repositories, added unit tests proving the guarded update statements, and added DB-backed characterization tests proving a concurrent completion is not overwritten by the stale reset sweep. | Apply the same update-time ownership fence to any future stale-recovery or retry-reset path that first selects rows and then updates them later. Do not rely on the stale scan alone under contention. | Evidence: [CR-241-STALE-RESET-OVERWRITE-RACE-REVIEW.md](./CR-241-STALE-RESET-OVERWRITE-RACE-REVIEW.md); replay/valuation/aggregation repository changes; targeted unit suite => `29 passed`; DB-backed overwrite race proofs for replay, valuation, and aggregation; OpenAPI gate and touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |

| CR-242 | 2026-03-14 | Terminal ownership fence for worker side effects | Hardened | Even after CR-241 fenced stale reset sweeps, late workers could still finish after losing ownership of a `PROCESSING` row. That left a second race: timeout recovery could reset or fail a job, and a late worker could still emit terminal side effects or overwrite terminal status afterward. | Changed replay and valuation terminal status updates to require current `PROCESSING` ownership, changed aggregation terminal updates to do the same, made those update paths return whether ownership was actually claimed, and gated valuation, aggregation, and replay-worker completion side effects behind that claim. Added unit proofs for replay terminal fencing, valuation late-owner suppression, aggregation late-owner suppression, and replay-worker lost-ownership behavior. | Add DB-backed ownership-loss proofs for the most critical worker families where feasible. Keep applying the same ownership-first pattern anywhere a worker can publish durable side effects after a timeout or retry takeover. | Evidence: [CR-242-TERMINAL-OWNERSHIP-FENCE-REVIEW.md](./CR-242-TERMINAL-OWNERSHIP-FENCE-REVIEW.md); worker/consumer/repository updates; targeted unit suite => `35 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |

| CR-243 | 2026-03-14 | Concurrent reconciliation run dedupe proof | Hardened | `ReconciliationRepository.create_run(...)` already used the right optimistic pre-read plus `IntegrityError` fallback pattern for duplicate `dedupe_key` requests, but that behavior had not been proved under real concurrent sessions. The control path was relying on structure rather than contention evidence. | Added a repository unit test proving the `IntegrityError` fallback returns the existing run, and added a DB-backed two-session integration test that forces both callers past the pre-read before insert and proves one durable run is created, one caller receives `created=True`, one receives `created=False`, and both receive the same `run_id`. | Apply the same DB-backed contention-proof pattern to other durable dedupe/upsert paths, especially instrument reprocessing triggers and valuation job upserts. | Evidence: [CR-243-CONCURRENT-RECONCILIATION-DEDUPE-PROOF.md](./CR-243-CONCURRENT-RECONCILIATION-DEDUPE-PROOF.md); reconciliation repository unit test; DB-backed concurrent dedupe integration proof; targeted pytest => `3 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |

| CR-246 | 2026-03-14 | Support overview control snapshot causality | Hardened | `get_support_overview(...)` fetched the latest financial reconciliation control stage and then separately asked for the "latest" reconciliation run for the same portfolio-day and epoch. Under changing state, one response could therefore mix a control row from one durable moment with a newer reconciliation run that did not yet exist when that control row was written. | Added an `as_of` fence to `get_latest_reconciliation_run_for_portfolio_day(...)`, filtered linked reconciliation runs by `started_at <= latest_control_stage.updated_at`, and updated the support overview to pass the control-stage snapshot time into the reconciliation lookup. | CR-281 | 2026-03-14 | Valuation status vocabulary contract alignment | Hardened | Query-service lineage/support DTO examples and some query-service tests still advertised completion status as `DONE`, while the durable runtime and repository-backed tests use `COMPLETE`. | CR-282 | 2026-03-14 | Support job skipped state truth | Hardened | Valuation jobs can durably end in `SKIPPED_NO_POSITION`, but the query-service support helper still collapsed that real outcome into `COMPLETED`. That made the support plane flatter and less truthful than the runtime state it was supposed to expose. | Updated support-job operational-state derivation to classify `SKIPPED*` statuses as explicit `SKIPPED`, widened the support-job DTO contract, added unit coverage for the helper branch, and added DB-backed integration proof that a real valuation support listing now exposes `SKIPPED_NO_POSITION` as skipped rather than completed. | Keep checking derived support states against durable runtime outcomes so real non-failure terminal states do not get flattened into generic success buckets. | CR-283 | 2026-03-14 | Outbox synchronous publish failure fence | Hardened | `OutboxDispatcher._process_batch_sync()` only treated delivery callbacks as failure inputs. If `KafkaProducer.publish_message(...)` raised synchronously for one row mid-batch, the dispatcher aborted before `flush(...)`, even though earlier rows in the same batch could already be queued in the producer. That left the batch unaccounted and risked ghost or duplicate delivery behavior on later flush cycles. | Fenced synchronous publish exceptions per row inside the batch loop, recorded those rows as failed delivery outcomes instead of aborting the whole batch, preserved `flush(...)` for already-queued rows, and added a DB-backed mixed-batch proof showing queued rows become `PROCESSED` while the synchronously failing row remains `PENDING` with `retry_count = 1`. | Keep reviewing producer-adjacent paths for failure modes that bypass callback-based accounting. At-least-once outbox delivery is only trustworthy if synchronous producer failures are turned into explicit durable outcomes instead of batch-wide aborts. | Evidence: [CR-283-OUTBOX-SYNCHRONOUS-PUBLISH-FAILURE-FENCE-REVIEW.md](./CR-283-OUTBOX-SYNCHRONOUS-PUBLISH-FAILURE-FENCE-REVIEW.md); outbox dispatcher update; outbox delivery-results integration test; targeted pytest and touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-284 | 2026-03-14 | Outbox flush-timeout accounting | Hardened | `OutboxDispatcher._process_batch_sync()` assumed that a non-exceptional `flush(...)` meant every queued row would eventually be represented in `delivery_ack`. In reality `flush(timeout=...)` can return a positive undelivered count without raising, leaving callback-less rows with no retry or failure accounting at all. | Treated `flush(...) > 0` as an explicit failure-accounting path for rows that still lacked delivery callbacks, preserved the normal retry/terminal-failure update flow for those rows, and added a DB-backed proof where one queued row gets a success callback, a second queued row gets none, `flush(...)` returns `1`, and the callback-less row remains `PENDING` with `retry_count = 1`. | Keep checking queue code for “no exception means fully accounted” assumptions. Producer timeout semantics often fail silently unless the batch logic converts callback-less rows into explicit retry outcomes. | Evidence: [CR-284-OUTBOX-FLUSH-TIMEOUT-ACCOUNTING-REVIEW.md](./CR-284-OUTBOX-FLUSH-TIMEOUT-ACCOUNTING-REVIEW.md); outbox dispatcher update; outbox delivery-results integration test; targeted pytest and touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-285 | 2026-03-14 | Ingestion batch partial publish truth | Hardened | `IngestionService` batch publish loops raised `IngestionPublishError` with only the first failing key. In a mid-batch Kafka publish failure, earlier records may already have been published and later records were never attempted, so ingestion job failure history under-described where the batch actually stopped. | Extended `IngestionPublishError` with `published_record_count`, added shared batch failure construction in `IngestionService`, and updated all ingestion batch publishers to persist the full remaining unpublished tail in `failed_record_keys` rather than just the first failing key. Added unit and integration proofs that both the raised error and the stored ingestion-job failure history now reflect the unpublished remainder of the batch. | If we need deeper ingestion observability later, the next step is structured batch-progress metadata such as published count and remaining unpublished count. | CR-286 | 2026-03-14 | Portfolio bundle publish progress truth | Hardened | `publish_portfolio_bundle(...)` fans one mixed request into multiple domain publish paths, but on failure the raised `IngestionPublishError` only described the failing sub-publish. That lost causal context about which earlier entity groups had already been emitted and which later groups were never reached. | Added per-entity `published_counts` tracking inside `publish_portfolio_bundle(...)` and wrapped inner `IngestionPublishError` instances with a bundle-level message that includes the already-published entity-group counts at the moment the bundle stopped, while preserving the original `failed_record_keys` and `published_record_count`. | CR-287 | 2026-03-14 | Reprocessing publish accounting | Hardened | `/reprocess/transactions` and the event-replay ingestion retry path both published directly to Kafka with duplicated local loops and `flush(timeout=5)`. | CR-288 | 2026-03-14 | Transaction replay republish accounting | Hardened | `ReprocessingRepository.reprocess_transactions_by_ids(...)` republished completed transaction events directly to Kafka in a loop and then called `flush()`. | CR-289 | 2026-03-14 | Scheduler dispatch flush accounting | Hardened | `ValuationScheduler._dispatch_jobs(...)` and `AggregationScheduler._dispatch_jobs(...)` still used direct `publish_message(...)` loops followed by bare `flush(timeout=10)`. | CR-290 | 2026-03-14 | DLQ publish flush accounting | Hardened | `BaseConsumer._send_to_dlq_async(...)` published a DLQ message, called `flush(timeout=5)`, and then immediately recorded the DLQ event. Because `flush(...)` can return a positive undelivered count without raising, the consumer could persist and log DLQ success before Kafka had actually acknowledged the DLQ message. | Treated positive `flush(timeout=5)` results as an explicit failure inside `_send_to_dlq_async(...)`, skipped durable DLQ-event recording on that path, and reused the existing fatal log branch for both flush-timeout and synchronous publish failure. | CR-291 | 2026-03-14 | DLQ commit gating | Hardened | `BaseConsumer.run()` treated terminal processing failure as “send to DLQ, then commit offset,” while `_send_to_dlq_async(...)` swallowed DLQ publication failure and only logged it. That meant the base consumer could fail processing, fail to publish to DLQ, and still commit the original Kafka offset, creating a real message-loss path. | Changed `_send_to_dlq_async(...)` to return explicit success/failure truth, updated `BaseConsumer.run()` to commit terminal-message offsets only when DLQ send succeeded, and added unit proofs that successful DLQ send still commits while failed DLQ send leaves the offset uncommitted for Kafka redelivery. | Keep checking any recovery or safety wrapper that still treats “logged recovery attempt” as equivalent to “durably succeeded.” Commit decisions should depend on real delivery success, not on best-effort send attempts. | Evidence: [CR-291-DLQ-COMMIT-GATING-REVIEW.md](./CR-291-DLQ-COMMIT-GATING-REVIEW.md); kafka consumer update; kafka consumer unit tests; targeted pytest => `12 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-292 | 2026-03-14 | DLQ replayer commit gating | Hardened | `tools/dlq_replayer.py` replayed the original message from a DLQ record, called `flush(timeout=5)`, logged success, and committed the DLQ offset. Because positive `flush(...)` results were ignored, the tool could fail to get replay delivery confirmation and still commit away the recovery opportunity. | Treated positive `flush(timeout=5)` results as an explicit replay failure in `DLQReplayConsumer.process_message(...)`, so the tool now commits the DLQ message only after replay delivery is actually accounted for. Added integration proof that a timeout leaves the DLQ message uncommitted, because rerunning the tool with the same consumer group replays the same message again successfully. | Keep applying the same delivery-accounting standard to recovery tooling, not just app services. Operator tools are part of the safety story, and they should not be more lossy than the runtime they are meant to recover. | Evidence: [CR-292-DLQ-REPLAYER-COMMIT-GATING-REVIEW.md](./CR-292-DLQ-REPLAYER-COMMIT-GATING-REVIEW.md); DLQ replayer update; tool integration tests; targeted pytest => `3 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-293 | 2026-03-14 | Replay publish truth after bookkeeping failure | Hardened | The ingestion replay endpoints used one broad try/except across Kafka publish plus later retry-state and audit writes. If Kafka replay succeeded but bookkeeping failed, the system flattened that outcome into generic failed, and duplicate-block lookup could miss that the replay had already been published. | Split both replay flows into publish and post-publish bookkeeping phases, added a truthful replay audit status `replayed_bookkeeping_failed`, updated duplicate-block lookup to treat that status as already-published success, and tightened unit/integration proofs around the new operator contract. | Keep checking recovery and remediation flows for places where Kafka publish success and later state persistence are still collapsed into one outcome. | CR-296 | 2026-03-14 | Ingestion shutdown flush truth | Hardened | Ingestion-service shutdown always logged Kafka producer flush success and ignored the return value of `producer.flush(timeout=5)`. | CR-297 | 2026-03-14 | Reprocessing tool flush truth | Hardened | `tools/reprocess_transactions.py` logged replay success before evaluating its final `flush(timeout=10)` result. Because the repository can queue earlier publishes before a later failure, that final flush is part of delivery accounting, not just cleanup, and the tool could overstate recovery success. | Added `_flush_or_raise(...)`, moved success logging behind a zero-undelivered final flush, and kept failure-path flush as best-effort cleanup that does not mask the original replay error. | CR-298 | 2026-03-14 | Worker and scheduler shutdown interruptibility | Hardened | `ReprocessingWorker`, `ValuationScheduler`, and `AggregationScheduler` only flipped `_running = False` on shutdown. If stop arrived while they were sleeping between polls, runtime teardown could stall for the full poll interval even though no more useful work remained. | Added `_stop_event` to all three long-poll loops, made `stop()` set both the flag and the event, and replaced bare `asyncio.sleep(...)` with interruptible stop-event waits so shutdown exits immediately after the current poll work completes. Added direct unit proofs that all three loops stop promptly even with long poll intervals. | Review any remaining long-poll runtime component that still treats shutdown as `set flag -> wait for next timeout`, especially outside these three core loops. | Evidence: [CR-298-WORKER-SCHEDULER-SHUTDOWN-INTERRUPT-REVIEW.md](./CR-298-WORKER-SCHEDULER-SHUTDOWN-INTERRUPT-REVIEW.md); worker/scheduler loop updates; targeted pytest => `32 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-299 | 2026-03-14 | Outbox dispatcher shutdown interruptibility | Hardened | `OutboxDispatcher` only flipped `_running = False` on shutdown and then waited for the next poll sleep to expire. If stop arrived just after a batch finished, runtime teardown could stall for the full poll interval even though no more outbox work remained. | Added `_stop_event` to `OutboxDispatcher`, made `stop()` set both the flag and the event, and replaced bare `asyncio.sleep(...)` in `run()` with an interruptible stop-event wait so dispatcher shutdown exits promptly after the current batch completes. | CR-300 | 2026-03-14 | Consumer commit failure DLQ misclassification | Hardened | `BaseConsumer.run()` handled successful message processing and synchronous offset commit in the same `try` block. If the message was processed correctly but `commit(...)` failed, the code fell into the terminal-processing failure path and attempted to send the message to DLQ, incorrectly treating broker/commit instability as poison-message evidence. | Split processing and commit into separate success phases, moved commit into the `else` branch after successful processing, and changed commit failure handling to log warning and leave the offset uncommitted for Kafka redelivery without sending the message to DLQ. Added a direct unit proof that commit failure no longer triggers DLQ publication. | Review any higher-level wrapper that still conflates broker/commit failures with terminal business-message failures after this base consumer fix. | Evidence: [CR-300-CONSUMER-COMMIT-FAILURE-DLQ-MISCLASSIFICATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-300-CONSUMER-COMMIT-FAILURE-DLQ-MISCLASSIFICATION-REVIEW.md); kafka consumer update; targeted pytest => `13 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-301 | 2026-03-14 | DLQ commit failure runtime fence | Hardened | Even after CR-300, the terminal-error path still committed offsets directly after successful DLQ publication. If that commit raised, the exception escaped the branch and could crash the consumer task even though DLQ publication had already succeeded. | Wrapped the post-DLQ commit in its own fence, logged warning on commit failure, left the offset uncommitted for Kafka redelivery, and prevented task-wide crash or reclassification of the message. | CR-302 | 2026-03-14 | Consumer shutdown flush fence | Hardened | `BaseConsumer.shutdown()` called `consumer.close()` and `producer.flush()` without any timeout accounting or exception fence. | CR-304 | 2026-03-14 | Bounded runtime shutdown | Hardened | `shutdown_runtime_components(...)` claimed to guarantee bounded shutdown but simply awaited `asyncio.gather(*tasks, return_exceptions=True)`. The shared shutdown evidence therefore existed in code but not at the service boundary where operators would actually look for it. | Updated all service `ConsumerManager` call sites that invoke `shutdown_runtime_components(...)` to pass `logger=logger`, then validated representative runtime-manager packs across persistence, aggregation, valuation orchestrator, and pipeline orchestrator surfaces. | Add a service-level assertion later if we want explicit proof that a shutdown callback failure is emitted through a service logger, not just that logger propagation is wired. | Evidence: [CR-306-RUNTIME-SHUTDOWN-LOGGER-PROPAGATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-306-RUNTIME-SHUTDOWN-LOGGER-PROPAGATION-REVIEW.md); consumer-manager call-site updates across services; representative runtime pytest => `8 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-307 | 2026-03-14 | Kafka producer close flush truth | Hardened | `KafkaProducer.close()` flushed and discarded the shared producer with no timeout accounting or exception fence. | CR-308 | 2026-03-14 | Worker runtime startup failure classification | Hardened | `run_instrumented_worker_service(...)` only wrapped `manager.run()` in its shared critical-error path. If Prometheus instrumentation setup failed before the manager started, the service crashed without the standard worker-runtime critical log. | Moved metrics instrumentation into the shared `try/except` so startup instrumentation failure is now classified through the same service-level critical path as runtime crashes, while still re-raising and emitting the shared shutdown log. Added a direct unit proof for instrumentation-startup failure. | If we want richer lifecycle evidence later, add explicit startup-stage labeling in the critical path. The immediate classification gap is now closed. | Evidence: [CR-308-WORKER-RUNTIME-STARTUP-FAILURE-CLASSIFICATION-REVIEW.md](./CR-308-WORKER-RUNTIME-STARTUP-FAILURE-CLASSIFICATION-REVIEW.md); worker runtime update; targeted pytest => `3 passed`; touched-surface `ruff check` passed. |
| CR-309 | 2026-03-14 | Kafka topic verification library failure classification | Hardened | `ensure_topics_exist(...)` was shared library code but called `sys.exit(1)` on unexpected metadata-verification failures. | CR-311 | 2026-03-14 | Runtime failure attribution ordering | Hardened | `wait_for_shutdown_or_task_failure(...)` selected an arbitrary completed task when multiple runtime tasks finished together. That could misattribute a real failure to an unrelated cancellation or clean exit if they landed in the same `done` set. | Changed task selection ordering to prefer exception-bearing failures first, then cancelled tasks, then clean exits. | CR-324 | 2026-03-14 | Shared lineage whitespace normalization fence | Hardened | Shared `normalize_lineage_value(...)` only treated exact `""` and `"<not-set>"` as unset. Whitespace-only values or padded sentinel values could therefore leak through as fake correlation, request, or trace ids across HTTP middleware, logging, and repository lineage persistence. | Changed shared lineage normalization to strip whitespace, treat empty-after-strip and case-insensitive `<not-set>` as unset, and return trimmed real lineage values. | CR-326 | 2026-03-15 | Container build baseline hardening | Hardened | `lotus-core` already had multi-stage service Dockerfiles, but the build baseline still carried an underspecified `.dockerignore` and no explicit BuildKit/buildx enablement in Docker-backed CI jobs. | CR-488 | 2026-05-28 | Cost-basis lot input invariants | Hardened | FIFO and average-cost strategies relied on caller validation for BUY lot quantity and costs. Direct strategy calls from initialization, repair, replay, or future loaders could admit dirty negative quantities or negative cost basis and corrupt available quantity, lot cost-per-share, and later realized P&L. | Added shared buy-lot input validation for cost-basis strategies: require calculated base/local costs, reject non-positive quantity except zero-quantity/zero-cost no-op lots, reject negative cost basis, and use normalized Decimal values for lot state. No route shape, database migration, wiki source, or platform contract change was required. | Evidence: [CR-488-COST-BASIS-LOT-INPUT-INVARIANTS.md](./CR-488-COST-BASIS-LOT-INPUT-INVARIANTS.md); `src/services/calculators/cost_calculator_service/app/cost_engine/processing/cost_basis_strategies.py`; focused cost-basis strategy proof => `14 passed`; cost-calculator unit pack => `115 passed`; warning gate => `2354 passed`, zero warnings; touched-surface `ruff check` and `ruff format --check` passed; `git diff --check` passed. |
| CR-489 | 2026-05-28 | Sell quantity disposition guards | Hardened | Dirty in-memory SELL events or direct average-cost strategy calls could carry negative sell quantities. The average-cost path could mutate holdings upward and return distorted cost-of-goods-sold before the caller detected invalid consumed quantity. | Added a SELL strategy quantity guard before available-quantity and lot-consumption calls, and added strategy-level negative sell quantity guards for FIFO and average-cost disposition.
